O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have finished this book which is the latest fruit of the science of medicine, and I have completed it by its demonstrations and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to my mind that I shall accompany this treatise with another part of the work of hands, namely surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is rare in our region and is strange to all, if it is not known and learned, and if only the small descriptions in the books of the ancients remain, which the hands have done
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And thus comes the error and the emptiness, and are closed the understandings and is aligned the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I shall make it alive altogether the order of this physician in accordance with the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I shall come together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is worth noting that none of the great masters of hands is found in our time; therefore the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus says Hippocrates that we must not fear what is not, but rather what is; and in the arts also.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We are told in the opening of this book that he who is ignorant of the things to be foretold should fear nothing that is unknown, but rather what is known; for I have often seen more harm done by those who are familiar with this science than by those who depart from it and its principles.</start_of_turn>
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish man who, having copped a scrophule or a woman’s neck, has cut the veins of the neck; and as much blood has issued from this as would fill a woman’s hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another evil which treats a stone of a bladder, and the stone was great; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and was dead for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I have already been called to treat, and I saw the condition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and I knew well if it were cut out, it would die.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another evil which treats a stone of our land which had the limb broken, and with the splinter it caused an injury; and the physicians of our land are compelled by strong constraint to leave the fracture above the wound, and do not allow any bleeding, and leave it until the end; and they command that it not be loosened again; and when the limb was entirely freed and the splinter was gone, it was lost.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I beseech you to come here, and I hasten to come and loosen the limb; and when I see it dislocated, it is at peace and does not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way the corruption is already confirmed or the limb is unsound, and it cannot be healed; and it does not cease until the corruption goes away from the limb as long as the limb is completely lost
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another remedy which is useful for the swelling of the veins is to apply a blistering salve or poultice which is made with the malice of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a wound that is caused by melancholy humours, it is only useful to touch it with fire if it is not in a limb where one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, indeed, you must know that the work of hands is become into twelve divisions: that is to say, there is peril in many positions; and I will show in each chapter where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For you must know that your hands must always be wary, lest the fools speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take up your arms carelessly, and undertake your ailments lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you may come out whole and sound; and leave the contagious diseases far behind with wholesome health; and keep your arms from that which makes you doubt, and have confidence that you will reach the other world in glory
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	The wicked spirits whisper to the sick: "Do not take care of your maladies, for you are not worthy of such treatment."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in two chapters
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and surgical instruments in general, from the head to the toes; and about the forms of instruments, and of the implements of cautery, and all that is necessary for the work
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with amputation and incision, of abscesses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and concerning the order of instruments and their forms.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the chief down to the feet, and from the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we have remembered from our work, it is necessary to say what is the quality of the aid and the great care of chest complexion
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the great care, is the longest word and the subtlest science and the greatest secret response; and of this they speak more of the sages, and they agree with this; and I find that their words are burdensome, for I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery helps universally to all complexion or where there is matter, for there are two complexions: that is to say a complexion hot and matter, and a complexion dry and matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche, matters assembled, some declare that the cautery is a great aid; others declare that the cautery is of no avail in diseases except those caused by heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it must not be the cure for hot diseases by heat, nor for drought; and thus those who say the opposite that the cautery does great aid in hot and dry diseases that arise from the humours of the body
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I consent to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never seen it happen otherwise by experience.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in every way, I know of no other way than that which has been shown by experience, since I have known by long experience the physician of cauteries, and the diversity of humoral complexions, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the results and remedies of their treatments; for other complexions we have no experience, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And you must all acknowledge and agree to the cautery.</start_of_turn
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, friends, that fire cautery is more effective for certain diseases than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery is simple, and brings no excessive heat except to the part that is being treated, and does not harm any other part besides that to which it is applied.</start_of_turn>
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another in their course, and cause the disease of grief to the member with the greatest suffering; and by chance they bring about the harm to the patient.</start_of_turn>
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, on account of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not make this [pain] worse, if there is no excess.</start_of_turn
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And thus I have learned through experience and the length of my service and study in this art, and I believe in its truth; for this is what philosophers have shown in demonstrating. Therefore I apologize for the length of my words, for it troubles me not that I must repeat what is secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of work, as it banishes diseases from the body, as the philosopher has said. Or you may consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know then, son, when the cauteries must be made and when they should be renounced.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is useful in all tensions, for the harmful things that arise are expelled by the help of the cautery; and even if the cautery is for necessary pains that are pressing and urgent and cannot wait until the greater harm has passed from the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, my son, that because fools make light of this matter; for the disease which is cured by cautery has no remission; and he says so himself; but it is not so simple as that, for cautery is but a medicine which moves the complexion and dries up humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for its haste, and for the excellence of its work and its sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And know that the disease never comes according to the complexion of the patient and the root of the disease and its virtue; and are gathered in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if these are not administered with cautery in place or if there is much superfluity and moisture, for the cautery is of no avail for pain, and the similar things, and part of the pain does not return; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that because cautery is called the last of medicine, and so it seems; but they do not believe that cautery is worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false, for it is the last of medicine because when we have administered various treatments for any disease and they have not been of avail, then we administer cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, although cautery is at the rear of medicine, it is not as the fools of this age believe.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients say that gold cautery is more merciful than iron, and they do not say that fire is harmful except for the quality of the gold and the fineness of its substance; and they say that the smell of the cautery does not cause harm, but this is not true, for I have proved it, and I have seen that it is seen in many people; and gold cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is charred by the color of the gold and how much it has cooled; and if you burn it too much, it will be ruined; and there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery, as we have learned it to be useful in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from the head downwards, forasmuch that the patient will be more comfortable finding them
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are useful both for moisture and for cold, and there are two kinds which are made for the cause of a disease which is called "soda", and for the cause of many humors which descend from the head as sweat, and on the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pains of the teeth and throat, and even for all diseases which come from cold as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a medicinal solution modifying the head, either twice or thrice, according to what is useful and agreeable and the custom of the patient; and then restore the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then set it comfortably between your hands, and put his hands over his stomach; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his thumb between his two eyes; and there will come out his two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the base then cover the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and do descending and extracting your hand somewhat forward and backward; then keep your hand steadily, and renew the cautery until you see the bone somewhat; and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that take up one fourth of an inch of solder, and put in awe and soft cotton inside, and take out the bone, and leave it for two days; after that put on a soft bandage on the outside; and leave on it until the swelling is gone. Then cure the wound of the swelling which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the ancients, the more time the wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason we must apply pressure.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must leave the cautery on for so long that any part of the bone is scorched, and then we must rejoin what is burnt of the bone and it must be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say another that we must leave the cautery on for so long that it is as wide as a woman’s girdle; and we must press so hard that the bone is forced out as wide as a woman’s girdle; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; and then we must cure and bandage it.</start_of_turn
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterizing do not seem to me to be suitable for all bones, for in some men or when there is pain; and I seem to think that I must leave it; for the head of the shoulder is easily dislocated by continuous solutions of the body, as we have seen in other members; and even when the head of the shoulder is weak by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more salve and milder for me, and in this way I shall obtain greater health.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain in the head that lasts a long time, the physician should use leech herbs, pills called "cochie", and vomiting of the head, oils, and poultices; and if we do the cautery as we have said above, it is of no use.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that if the patient's pain is strong and not too severe; then burn the cautery only as much as we have said above.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have burned the cautery on the skin of the head up to the bone, as we have said, and you have burned the vein which is called "vasselz"; and that is where we put sponges; and hold your hand so that you do not see blood until the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this burn than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is better to burn the hair close to the root than to burn the middle of the hair, and that is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the shoulder there is sudden pain, and the disease is widespread, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by medicines that modify it, and other cures have been made as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this brings no benefit: then one must make cauteries according to two methods, namely with vinegar and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The vinegar cautery is as follows: if you take a spoonful of vinegar and apply it to the skin, the eschar will be loosened and the burn will be removed. If there are two bones involved, do the same with the temple where the pain is located until you can rejoin the spoonful of vinegar under the skin; and when it is rejoined, bind and stretch it well and leave it for 12 hours; then remove it and treat the burn with garlic, and leave the wound open for one or two days; then put on a bandage as much as is necessary for support.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of the swelling while it is still sane; and if you see that you do nothing of the medicines I have written or dose them with other medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is according to this manner. Heat the cautery so that it is of this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a cup or it has a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small mark; and put out the painful limb, and hold your hand and slightly withdraw the fire until half of the thickness of the hair is burned; and keep your hand away from the artery, which must not be burned, and there will be plenty of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton wool over the wound, take out the limb by .iij. days; then put moist cotton wool in the wound, and then cure the limb of swelling until it is healed. And if you wish to cauterize this embolism with the cautery which is called "cultellare", at the tip, and keep the artery in this embolism which is not the ancient one.
de emigraine	After placing cotton wool over the wound, take out the limb by .iij. days; then put moist cotton wool in the wound, and then cure the limb of swelling until it is healed. And if you wish to cauterize this embolism with the cautery which is called "cultellare", at the tip, and keep the artery in this embolism which is not the ancient one.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure an embolism as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does no good, and you see that the cautery must precede medical treatment and that it will not suffice, then you must avoid the cautery which is called "cultellare" as long as it is blunt; and sign out the limb by drawing a line half an inch long, and hold your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and that no blood vessel comes loose; and take care of the jaw that it does not move when you move it, and that it does not move more than the movement of the muscle and spasm does to the patient; and take care of the discoloration of blood from the artery when it is cut, or when it is cut there is great fear and doubt about it, and that is not studied and experienced; and leave the work half done; but I will tell you later how to retain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the surrounding area as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of scissors; and this cautery is better than the former and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	If you see that this cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the surrounding area as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of scissors; and this cautery is better than the former and more helpful.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and we have applied various healing medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then you must apply this cautery which is called the “pinch,” for this is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the painful ear, or around the two joints if the pain persists in both, and you have loosened a piece from the root of the ear as soon as you have signed the mark; and there are ten points around the ear; after that, cure the mark until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	After pricking all around the painful ear, or around the two joints if the pain persists in both, and you have loosened a piece from the root of the ear as soon as you have signed the mark; and there are ten points around the ear; after that, cure the mark until it is healed.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is not fierce except for those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cautery which appears to come from drying and swelling of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture which is made of fumes of hydras and purges of head and gargling, it is worth nothing; therefore you must cauterize the patient with two cautery irons: one at the root of the ear, and the other at the temple, and the third between the two eyebrows; and put the cautery on the part which opens well, and make the cautery under the head of the ear below a little distance from the corner of the eye, and another at the temple as long as a bean; and leave the cautery on until half of the hair is burnt; and that is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the like of a cutlass which we have shown you before is made, but it is a more subtle and effective remedy than the knife should be a larger one; after curing like this as I have said above, as long as it is not harmful.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it as we have said above, and it does not profit, and the patient does not have fever, then you must make three cauteries: one on each corner of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the vessel which is called the «vasselz» as we have said above, and the last cauterize on the mouth of the stomach; and be cured as we have said above.
de litargie	De litargie.

When lying down. S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit. If you see me add more, and the patient is suffering, I make another cautery in the middle; and if the patient is well, two more on the two corners, and the wound is to be treated until it is healed. de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	From the coldness of the head, it must be that the head be loosened from the hair and from what has been said previously; after raising the patient’s head, then make the cautery immediately on the head and on the beard, that is to say behind and before the eyebrow; and if you must do more, and the limb is moist and the patient is pale, and the disease is violent, make three cauteries on the eyebrow of the back; and leave them as long as the patient can bear it, and keep your hand steady; after the cure while it is still sound, and is the cautery which is called “olivare” which has been mentioned previously.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epilentiques must only use fire cautery when the patient is feverish; and first modify the hair of the head and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and suffering from excessive medical care.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit. Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is young, make .i. subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When melancholy is the cause, superabundance or corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then you must cauterize with some of the cauteries as we have said for the paralyzed patient.

After that, take the chief of the sick person; then make a circle of lint well made, as much as a circle, and put it around the chief; and hold the patient’s limbs crossed, and keep them firmly held from all sides; then present the dressing, and moisten it with old alum; and put the fire to the temper, so that it should not suffer too much; then drain the circle from within the chief, and let it cool down; do this to the sick person every week once with another good treatment, until he is healed
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline. de l’awe des eulz	Or if thou seest cauterize the head in making many points at all the cautery. This manner of cautery doth diminish the cerebrum immediately; and then put upon moist cotton in burrow and in grease of geline.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe first comes, as eulz by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and do give the patient something to drink that will temper the head, and keep it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more times when fasting.

After he has been commanded to reinsert his head, and when he has made cautery at the head, and has made thirteen cauteries upon the two temples when they descend from the brow to the two eyes together, or if they descend from the brow alone; and close at the end of the cautery all the veins and arteries that are beside the ear, and that the cautery should be long in proportion to the width of the temple; and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood isse, if it is stained with parts of blood as you have.

dou cors des larmes	except for tears.

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or bleed the arteries that are in appearance near the brow; and it is seen that these are cold, fleumatic superfluities, then make the cautery as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, that is to say: cautery of the brow and two cauteries on the two temples and two cauteries or to ligate the two bones; and if necessary, make a further cautery below the eye at the root of the nose with a small cautery.

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the moisture of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery which is called "olivare" is used. Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit. dou poil qui point l’oil	because of the hair which points the oil.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never fail that when the hairs of the oil have become converted to the beard, prick the oil, and make cautery in three ways: that is, of fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Never fail that when the hairs of the oil have become converted to the beard, prick the oil, and make cautery in three ways: that is, of fire or burning medicine. For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal, then place the patient in a comfortable position; after that mark on the skin the figure that is like that of a sparrow's feather or like the beginning of a sign from the hairs; then put a moist cloth on the oil and a poultice of persillain on top, and then burn the cautery as follows:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked and several times, that the hair should be as dark as possible in that place; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the master retreat, and the hair is raised to the point of the oil; then take your hand away, and leave it be for two days, and put a moist cloth over the wound until the swelling has subsided; then cure it with oil until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hair comes out, and the master is softened, then repeat the cautery on the same place as before; and if the hair is plucked out, if the cautery is done so that the master returns to its natural position, and is even, and does not prick the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you command the patient to leave the hair long and even, then make a parchment of the shape of the ivy leaf; then take frankincense and live charcoal, each a third, and grind them together well; and make it hot, if it does not cool down, and put on the shape that you have made like the ivy leaf, and put the master on the wound with eggs; and if the disease persists with only oil, one must open in one, and if in both; and put cotton soaked in oil on the wound.  And the head of the patient should be in its normal position and put your thumb showing on the medicine, and press it once or twice every time the patient feels the bite of the medicine, because he feels the bite as well as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the bones of medicine are at your disposal.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the biting is passed, if you lift up the limb, and behold if the wound is raised just as high as it was raised by the contraction of fire or by incision; and if it is firm, it is well. If not, if you must repeat the medicine upon the limb or the medicine has not worked, until your works are equal, and your wounds are set to their place; then put on a wet cloth in the wound until the pulse is calm, and then cure the limb of the swelling which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you must stay with great care so that no medicine is lost from your wound, and if the pulse becomes faint after the bite, and the hair pricks in the oil, if you must repeat the medicine upon that limb which has become softened by the pulse, just as you did before; then cure until it is healed; and that is the form of the chaste dove.</start_of_turn
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to that which is your constraint; do not give the right answer to him who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to that which is your constraint; do not give the right answer to him who is studying this art.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	And know that when you cure fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cure does not profit, then you must burn it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in your health; and hold his ears between your hands in part that they do not move, do not let them droop; then put cotton moistened with oil of rue or in vinegar on the wound; then burn the cautery that is partly: and is shaped like a pine cone, gather that it is the cautery; if you see, if it is pierced from one ear to the other, and if you see, if it is like a tent; but whatever, what is burned is worth more for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells over, and with the passage of time, it becomes soft; if it closes, if the swelling subsides, and there is a discharge of pus, then immediately apply the burn cautery, and keep your hand on the cautery over the area not covered by oil, so that your hands do not tremble; put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and hold it down.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you arrive at the beginning of the cautery treatment up to the bone, that would be good. If this does not happen, if you must repeat the cautery once more, and another time if necessary, and you leave it for two days; after that put on a moist bandage over the burn, and leave the healing of the desiccant oil until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and leave as the chapter dictates
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned. With the fistula open, and the limb fenestrated; after that put in the groove one half of a barleycorn of alum, which is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I make in quantity of a third of a pound; and keep your hand or forearm firmly closed, and do not move the patient in any way, until the melted wax has settled to its oil; and it is best to put it on the patient’s wound covered with a moist bandage of wool or linen: for if the wax is too soft it will be like a fistula, and too hard it will cause great marvel for cleanliness.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if it is necessary, we can perform an incision on the nerve and bring the fistula back to its proper place as it should be in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	from cracks in the bones
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur fractures in bones that are called "hair," and sometimes in bones of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you have cured these fractures as we have said in the divisions, and the cure does not help, then you must perform a small incision with a cautery as follows:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the patient immediately on those fractures until they are healed; after curing the limb until it is whole again.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the armpit.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When a boil comes up at the root of the toe or in the heel, or in the ankle or the root of the tooth, after that it becomes rotten and swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it will not profit you: therefore you must cauterize it according to the size of the fistula; after the burn or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until life returns to the front or behind it; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured once, it is good; and if this is not the case, if you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your treatise.
dou movement des dens	When a boil comes up at the root of the toe or in the heel, or in the ankle or the root of the tooth, after that it becomes rotten and swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the divisions, and it will not profit you: therefore you must cauterize it according to the size of the fistula; after the burn or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until life returns to the front or behind it; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured once, it is good; and if this is not the case, if you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your treatise.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you must cure it by medicine; this is of no use: therefore you must put the patient’s head in your hand; after that, withdraw the cautery as much as you like; and put into the cautery some hot mustard immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that, withdraw your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after that, fill the patient’s mouth with salt and keep it there for an hour and a quarter.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, when it is confirmed that it is moving, the head becomes soft and restrained, and the moisture corrupts and dries.
de la dolor des dens	And in this way, when it is confirmed that it is moving, the head becomes soft and restrained, and the moisture corrupts and dries out the pain of the teeth.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize in two ways: cautery of the burr and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If the burr is such that you take a burr of gutta, and you put a loop at the end on a sickle or pin; after that take cotton and wrap over the tip of a cloth, and moisten the burr well, and put on the tooth that aches immediately and hold until it is cooled; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see if there is still moisture left in the burr and cotton on the gut, and put on the tooth that aches, and put on the iron again until the fire comes to the edge of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is thus: take a piece of iron or charcoal as thick as a finger, and let it burn until the fire reaches the patient’s mouth; then quench the cautery, for when it forms it will harden; place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will soon be forgotten. Let the patient fill his mouth with saliva in the haste of this cautery, and then draw it out; this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	Do as you please with the cautery, as you wish; this is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	of scrofula.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is made of phlegm and cold moisture, and is not obedient to digestion by medicines, then evacuate the cautery from this place afterwards; and make four incisions for the fumes to escape from the cautery of the other side; and put the cautery hot upon the abscess once, or when mixing is complete, until it reaches the front of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in place for two days; and put upon it a moist dressing until the swelling is ossified; then cure the wound of abscesses and sutures until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores and is joined by a cold complexion, then it is recommended that the patient be first relieved by soluble medicines; after that perform the cautery at the root of the tongue, and hold it so that it does not go down to the throat, and do not burn more than necessary. Then perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone and the head of the scapula, which is called the "clavicle"; and cure the wound as we have said above until it is healed
de la toust	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores and is joined by a cold complexion, then it is recommended that the patient be first relieved by soluble medicines; after that perform the cautery at the root of the tongue, and hold it so that it does not go down to the throat, and do not burn more than necessary. Then perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone and the head of the scapula, which is called the "clavicle"; and cure the wound as we have said above until it is healed.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all fevers and diseases of the pores are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and the disease is ancient, let him undergo four cauteries on the forcele in the veins; and another cautery between two mammary glands; and let the cautery which is called "claw" be according to the form which is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	When you see that, perform a cautery at the place where the cautery called "points" is formed, if the form is as it is in the ear disease; and let the points extend to .xxx., or as much as necessary. After curing according to what is before said, and let the remaining cautery be twice according to this form.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, because you make two at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, support the patient on their back and chest; then grasp the thumb which is inside the armpit with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated, if necessary, withdraw the cautery which has about the size of a hazelnut
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	... and cauterize the thumb until it reaches the costae, and the escape of the cautery will be together three cauteries; and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery which has two nails, because the figures of cautering are these two nails; and the nerves are according to the sensitivity of a limb and this is the form of the cautery which has two nails.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is the suture adjusted upon this nerve for there are six cauteries upon it.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After putting on the cautery, broil the hairs with a needle; then rest the patient, and do not hold the limb tight so that it is tense until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated there, whatever the cause may be, then make a cautery upon the edge of the wound or several cauteries by pricking. For the joint is closed, and the moisture is dry, and the patient is healed
dou cautere de pleuresin	of pain.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient said that we must make at pleasure cauteries of the root of Aristotle, and in part: take a root of Aristotle long, the greatest that you will find, and be dry, and be as thick and as long as your thumbs; and the juice in oil, and the print at the fire, and cauterize. I. cauterize between the forefinger and the thumb, and II. a few cauteries one inch below the beard; and III. cauterize between the fifth rib and the hipbone, declining behind one inch. I. cauterize the spleen, and I. another on the stomach, and I. between two ribs, and II. have two ribs beside the spleen that push away the cautery that is between two ribs; and do not press me your hand, but make it open just as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And they say no ancient man uses a fire cautery resembling a scraper, and puts the scab and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to this incision; and leaps forth the pain, as we have said in the incision of the liver. But in this work is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	From mice.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse from what we have said concerning the divisions of the cures, and it does not help, then there remain two methods of cautery which are both good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	When you treat the disease of the mouse from what we have said concerning the divisions of the cures, and it does not help, then there remain two methods of cautery which are both good.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and another manner of cautery if the cautery which has three nerves is scraped off, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and hold the limb which is where the mouse is, or the wound of the patient comes from the left side, and let the elevation which you bind the limb with, according to the limb, according to the length of the bone, and the cautery be according to the breadth of the bone.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After that, if there are three hairs remaining unburned, let the fire touch them until they are perceived from the other side. Then withdraw the cautery quickly. And if you see that the hairs have been cauterized throughout, leave only two. After that, cure when the wound has undergone long tension, and this is worth as much as the other cures mentioned above.
de ydropisie	After that, if there are three hairs remaining unburned, let the fire touch them until they are perceived from the other side. Then withdraw the cautery quickly. And if you see that the hairs have been cauterized throughout, leave only two. After that, cure when the wound has undergone long tension, and this is worth as much as the other cures mentioned above.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The cautery is not effective for dropsy; except for the method which is called "asclytes". When you treat according to the methods that we have said in the divisions, and your cure does not help, then you must make three cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two on the back on the spine, and one on the buttock; and let the cautery be close to the hair's root.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery uncovered for a while to drain the wound, do not leave the dressing on the patient after the cautery; and healing will be expedited, and the wound will be completely rejoined with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the nail that we have before you shown; and for the back it is olive-shaped, as it is shown here.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the parts
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the parts are swollen in those who are hydro-pyic, and are filled with yellow bile, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the thumb between the thumb and the little finger; and hold your hand with the cautery towards that side. And do not enter too deeply with the point, because it would burn the yellow bile, and make the cautery in the fashion mentioned above:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two incisions in the groin of the leg at the point of the little toe; and let the incisions be long, one of them above the knee and the other below, in the leg; and leave the incisions open along their length to cure, that they may stay in place; after that, cure the other wounds that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	After that, make two incisions in the groin of the leg at the point of the little toe; and let the incisions be long, one of them above the knee and the other below, in the leg; and leave the incisions open along their length to cure, that they may stay in place; after that, cure the other wounds that we have mentioned.

de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain originates from a wound, call it "podagre" indeed; and when the cause is cold and medicines fail to cure it, it is often cured by cautery in part: make the opening of the cautery around the joint that is painful, and let the cautery be of olive oil in this fashion:

And if the pains are in the hands, if you make pricks around the nail one and a half lines; and if there remains no pain, if you make pricks on some joint and on the edge of the hand; and if the pains come up to the hips or to the elbows, if you cauterize some part, and give good instructions to the patient and prescribe medicines. For if you give good instructions and purge phlegm, health will be restored with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	From the root of the scapula

tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Until it is soft and it sweats sensations. And when you do not arrive at the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
