And I will tell you afterwards about the cure of the tail in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
de la routure dou ventre	of the route of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When other vents come round and are known, and you see that they do not grow further, then you must make a new cautery of the same quantity, and either a third of the former; after which treat according to what has been said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at two angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first mark the place well and make a line along the width of the vent, and another below, and hold your hand firmly over the cautery needle. But the first cauteries are lighter and softer.</start_of_turn>
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from a wound, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not worth it; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called the "points," or that the cautery be performed according to the length of the limb, its thinness and weakness, its toughness and its location of twists and pain. If it is successful on the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary that it should be repeated as close to the painful part as possible, for it is believed that the more cauteries are made, the sooner the patient will be healed.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from a wound, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not worth it; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called the "points," or that the cautery be performed according to the length of the limb, its thinness and weakness, its toughness and its location of twists and pain. If it is successful on the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary that it should be repeated as close to the painful part as possible, for it is believed that the more cauteries are made, the sooner the patient will be healed.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mesentery provides no aid at all by cautery with great help, and even the disease that comes from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy. Can you see it cauterized? Take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not linger, and you will doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the whole illness, then make five cauteries on the head: that is, one on the top of the head, and the other towards the front at the end of the beard; and two on each ear, and one behind on the cheek; and leave the hand as long as the cautery comes up to the bone, and as long as the edges come out strong so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize the head according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if there is widespread moisture everywhere, and it becomes manifest, if you command these cauteries that we have spoken of or chief, namely cauterize on the top of the thumb and index finger, and two on the elbow of the shoulder, and three on the elbow of the back, and one large on the wrist and one other below, and two on the two thumbs, and two on the scapulae, and two on the tendons of the wrist, and one on each joint of the fingers and toes, and on the recesses of the hands; take care that you do not burn the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, and do not make any cautery on the bones of the heel or the stomach or the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And the more cauteries you make, the more aid you provide, and the more beneficial it is; and the patients do not feel pain from the cautery as they feel it, because the flesh is already corrupted. It is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the members and joints, as you do in handling various things. After treatment, cover the area with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
de enfleure	of inflammation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and dressings, and is not completely healed, then you must perform cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either make the cautery a little deeper than the depth of the nerve which moves the limb; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And in no case must you perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of the nerve which moves the limb, and if it is bony the swelling will remain. And in no way should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the exits of the moving nerves.
de albaras	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and dressings, and is not completely healed, then you must perform cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either make the cautery a little deeper than the depth of the nerve which moves the limb; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And in no case must you perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of the nerve which moves the limb, and if it is bony the swelling will remain. And in no way should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the exits of the moving nerves.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and the remedies of medicine do not help, then you must cauterize with a needle a little deeper than the depth of the nerve, according to the quantity of the tissue; until the swelling is bony and changes color; then cure with flour of times and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and almond, each part a third; mix them all together, and bind with a bandage, and keep it in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for carbuncles by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a carbuncle starts, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the carbuncle. And all the wise men say that we should cauterize at the middle of the carbuncle; and all of them do not seem to me to be good, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already had to do it several times; and the right thing is that it be cauterized around, at the cautery which is called the "circle", as we have said concerning cauteries.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has an ailment that is called "adubelati," and it lingers without healing or because of its excessive production or because of the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and there is much blood, or for lack of tension; and you see it haste to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it be. For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce with all the cauteries, if the cautery is too hot: this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the nerve, and be such the cauteries that the patient feels relief in parts as the disease progresses. After that, cure as long as it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	The fire cautery. Another method for disease which is called "corrodens" is nothing other than the softening of a limb, because it makes the limb as dry as the lines of fire. If you see this disease in a limb which can suffer from whole-body cautery, then burn the small and great nails according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; after that cauterize all parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains except the bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the cauterized limbs, let them be broiled with oil until the burnings of the fire are ossified, and all the corruption. After the cure of the oily nourishment. And if after two days the limb is well, that is good; but if not, resume the cautery on what remains soft of the limbs corrupted. This softening is never cured by medical treatment in place of fire cautery; but every time fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The fire cautery. Another method for disease which is called "corrodens" is nothing other than the softening of a limb, because it makes the limb as dry as the lines of fire. If you see this disease in a limb which can suffer from whole-body cautery, then burn the small and great nails according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; after that cauterize all parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains except the bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the cauterized limbs, let them be broiled with oil until the burnings of the fire are ossified, and all the corruption. After the cure of the oily nourishment. And if after two days the limb is well, that is good; but if not, resume the cautery on what remains soft of the limbs corrupted. This softening is never cured by medical treatment in place of fire cautery; but every time fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that when a piece of flesh has departed from its natural place, a disease called "clos" arises, which is a great and burdensome thing that causes great suffering. And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways. That is, fire cautery and hot water cautery. For fire cautery, if you are callous, that is, if you cauterize carelessly like a quill over a piece of felt, it should be done with a piece of iron of the size that can penetrate the whole area and leave fine margins; then put all around the area over the area, and hold your hand firmly over the area until it comes to the front of the area; and leave it there for two days until it begins to swell; then make an ointment of bruised wild mallow seeds with beeswax, and leave the ointment on all night, and close the wound securely and remove the stitches from their roots. Then cure the wound cautiously.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	When it is converted by bloodstains, and many times occurs in the hands and on the feet, if you must perform hot water cautery; and this is partly in the method: take a sickle of iron or steel, or a quill of felt, and put it on the area and the surrounding area, that is, to cover the nails; then put the sickle on so that it covers everything around, then put some warm oil on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the edge of the sickle comes to the root of the area, and can find the warm water way down to the root; and give the patient a mouthful of warm water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will burst out all at its roots. Do this again until you have drained away all that is in the area, and then cure the wounds which cause swelling.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold, or from a quarter-fever or from another, if you make for him three or four cautceries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, one cautery or pinch, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave it like that, it will cause the sickness to depart quickly.
des pustules puans	When someone trembles from cold, or from a quarter-fever or from another, if you make for him three or four cautceries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, one cautery or pinch, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave it like that, it will cause the sickness to depart quickly.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever the body is covered with boils or pus-filled abscesses, which come from corrupted matter, if you make the first one to appear undergo cautery on each head of the abscess: a subtle cautery of fir-twig of Myrtle, from which the point is grasped by the fire, or of long Aristolochia root, or the lenticular cautery. And never should you cauterize until they first appear, following this method, for it does not burn through the fat before it, but ruptures the surplus from which they come, and brings relief; but you must do this after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to extend it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without calming the pain, and no blood comes out any more; then take the olive cautery and make several small and large burns until they are all red; then touch, that is to say, great or small as it is appropriate for the wound and the limb in which the artery is obstructed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is necessary to stop the bleeding
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you remove your thumb from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of another cautery that is on the fire immediately.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform this one after the other until the limb is stretched out; and beware that thou dost not tear away the nerve which is beneath, and that no other evil arise upon the patient; and keep that when without excision of the artery, one cannot well reattach the limb itself when the artery is large, except by three methods which we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by strong ligation of thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have power to reattach blood.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who brings about the restoration of the limb with great care is by the strict draping of cloths or the putting of things burning upon, or other similar things, if these do not profit, it is of no use.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no other remedy and there is no medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it steady until it is rested from the wound and from the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is as cold as the air until the wound is frozen and thickened and rested; and make incisions before that which must be cauterized and medicated.</start_of_turn>
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag li seconde livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to perform cautery of fire, or applied medicine, and the symptoms, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and in this chapter we shall speak of these matters from the head to the toes, for we have found it easier in this way to explain what we wish to convey.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must inform you, dear friend, that there is more peril and fear in this chapter than in all the previous cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake madness. For many people come to cures in this way. If they come from those who have suffered so much with their disease that they move lightly because of the force of their suffering, and from the greatness of their malice; from these things we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these things there are those who make you sense, and say: "Wait, I am a liar"; and the disease is desperate. It is not enough for me that you allow those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not recklessly believe me more than prudently of what you are certain, and of what you have taken and lost; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation may be either converted or obtained; and this will help you to ask for good renown, glory, and memory forever.</start_of_turn>
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lords, you do well to understand and approve, and if the Holy inspiration of his hand returns to you, amen.</start_of_turn>

dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded thee this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I had commanded thee from head to foot, forasmuch that ye shall find it more lightly what ye have to do.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	The sickness often comes from the swelling of the belly of the child, and when the navel is too tightly strained, the head of the child is often thrown off.  Never does this happen for any other reason than that it does not go back into place
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease vanish except in the countryside, and with all those whom I have seen, it hastens death; therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in parts for cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in childhood, when the shoulder was dislocated and the head swelled up so much that it could not be supported; and I believed that there was too much moisture, and this moisture if it is gathered in the bone above the socket, between the head and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the head and the bone, and the incision is small, you must make a wide incision; and as much as .ij. we have seen, until the moisture moves.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the form of a cross, following this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if moisture is on the bone, and you see the sinuses of the cheek swell out on the outer side, and it becomes taut when you press your hand inside, and this does not go back: if you suspect that the jaw is fractured, make two incisions according to this manner.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. And after the incision, drain out the moisture forcefully. After that, tighten the edges of the skin and fat, and apply wine and oil, and leave for five days; then remove the dressing, and cure the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the jaw completely still, and give the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look or open the orifice of the abscess, and the collection of pus; for it is never before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.

de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the injection of liquid, and you do as you please; keep away from the artery; let the vein flow blood, if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and moisture evacuation.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease that is called "catarrh" which has boils or swellings, and the disease is ancient, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last cure is to cauterize with this that we will cover the arteries.

de emigrainne	If the artery does not open despite feeling it, if you must measure the quantity of the space of two fingers, then mark it and keep it until the bone; and what is to be done with blood that must be put out if it is more than half full, and sometimes less or more, according to what the patient can suffer, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the bone where the stitches were placed, if the wound that was closed together does not move, then strain the wound and tie it, and cure it until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient secretion comes and acute catarrh, because of the tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient saliva forsened and similar things, it is treated by medical cures and other things that do not benefit it, if the arteries of the temples are extracted and cauterized, as we have said
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of extracting them is that if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating; and is not put back violently as in certain persons who are too rough.  If it is put back, the patient tightens his collar with some bandages, then wipes the limb of any rough hair, and raises the limb of warm water until the artery resumes its normal pulsation; then take the sponge and that which is the shape of a spatula.
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then loosen the skin lightly until you see the artery, then pull it up tightly with tweezers, and remove it well from the hair that remains on the root. For if it is not cut off, it will not rise without pain in all probability.</start_of_turn>
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Then drain blood from the groin to the navel, just over two fingers; and if the artery is large, it is prudent to ligate it with two strong threads of silk, so that no blood will remain below the support of the wound, and drain the blood; then cut away the excess that is between the two ligatures in that part, and if you see that there is still blood, cauterize with a small cautery until the hair is cut off; and that is the end of the operation, if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion.</start_of_turn>
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is helpful to finish off moisture: because of this it is of more great aid for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the fire cautery is useful for extracting arteries that are filled with much cotton and are placed under well-made stitches; and when they are loosened, if there is no cure for dry medicines that cause new blood vessels to grow, and stitches, until they are healed; and if the artery is not stopped as it should be with the cautery, or if you use too much of the cautery, the hand will be scorched; and if you do not have this present, if you must withdraw the hand, you must do so until the hand is no longer numb, and raise the hand with cold water until the sensation returns, and strain as it should be strained; and what is milder and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery through a cut of about one-third of an inch, but the cut should be well thick to prevent it from burning for a longer period.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the .ij. needles space one must have of great distance. Then when you have signed the .ij. loops, and you must let the loop burn over until it reaches the bone, and close the wound in .ij. loops; and be spaced out between the .ij. bones because it is not firmly soldered from this cautery in all. This is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	And must have between the two needles space one must have of great distance. Then when you have signed the two loops, and you must let the loop burn over until it reaches the bone, and close the wound in two loops; and be spaced out between the two bones because it is not firmly soldered from this cautery in all. This is the form of the cautery.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the test of the head of the sufferer, and it brings no relief from medicine what is being done, and you see the face of the patient to be swollen, and feels heat of the body if like a flame; and if there are tensed and moist if the papers are rough, and are chafed by the tears, and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is any hope of this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called him the 'old contusion' because you must make at the sick man who has this disease the hairs that he has on the front, then make two incisions or front equally according to the length of the front; and let one incision be as wide as two teeth downwards towards the belly, and the other let the other two edges be bound up with papers, and keep the incision of the arteries that are bound up with papers; and align your hand from the continuation of the two mandibles, and if there is any wound, take the quantity of two teeth that are at the passage of the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And show a piece of sponge and wipe with a cloth his blood, then withdraw the instrument sharply from the part where this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple down to the second incision; and remove all the bone that is between the two incisions to the very surface of the bone, then make the other half of the wound down to the other second, and then take out this instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the “cultellaire,” which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, does not penetrate deeply, and is smooth, that is the shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the “cultellaire,” which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, does not penetrate deeply, and is smooth, that is the shape. And place the handle of the cutting instrument towards the upper edge of the joint, and the blunt end towards the bone, and grasp firmly until it reaches the middle of the incision. And cut all the blood vessels that descend from the head as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the bone, and then finish the incision in the middle of the incision until the other edge; and then withdraw the needle equally, expressing the blood from the wound; then place in the wound a piece of cotton wool, and cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil and herbs, and keep that there are no afterbleeds. And after three days remove the dressing, and introduce great plant material of aquaphore, then cure with basic oil of rose, and other cures which are used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	because of the return of the blood vessels
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is done, and you see the eyes tense and small, and the pupil dilates, and the papers burn; the hair cries out, and where it breaks off, there is great pain, and the patient vomits; then the discharge from these causes is greater than from many veins, and the cure is that which is.

En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Whatever is causing the swelling of the ears is one of three things: grains of sand, pieces of metal, stones, or other such things; seeds, such as peas, beans, or barley; or pus, which is watery and foul smelling.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a stone or other foreign body in the ear that does not fit into the ear, do not attempt to remove it from the ear, but place the ear under the sun. If you see the stone, if no violet oil or oil of lavender is secreted, then perform an extraction; and let the patient sneeze out any congealed blood, and wipe away the blood from the nose when he sneezes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear down. Many times this cure will cause blood to flow; and if it does not flow, an extraction with fine needles must be performed. For this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it bursts out with needles, that is good; if not, perform an extraction with fine needles; and if it does not burst with the needle, make a scar on the side of the ear or remove a large part of the ear, and wipe away what is around the scar with butter if it comes out without the needle; then the blood will flow, for often it comes out by itself; and if it does not come out in this way, take hold of the testicles and put on no instrument that can cause damage, and put a plug of cotton in; then press on the testicles above the stone or whatever it is, and the blood will flow.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in haste to make an incision, do not hesitate to perform the incision above the earlobe as well as on the abscess. Incise the earlobe cautiously first, making the initial incision at the crown of the head; let blood escape according to its quantity. Then hold the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, make a small incision at the root of the earlobe, either at the fat or the cartilage. The incision should be as wide as a moon until you reach the bone, and then remove the bone as much as you are able. Exude the pus from your mouth and leave the wound until it has healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the grain is swollen and painful, administer extraction; if it cannot be extracted, administer a sponge tencel soaked in vinegar in this fashion:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But make no incision until you think the grain is softened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many attempts; then extract it with tweezers and soak in vinegar, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When the ear is acute, then the patient should at once apply a compress to the ear and fill the ear with wool. And be it without or with the acute being within the ear itself; if it should burst by this, that is good. If not, take many pins according to the length of your finger should tension and support, and push them one by one into the fire; and put the patient one or two of his ears into the fire, and pull out from the other side, and fix one pin on the pin which is in the ear; and do this until the acute is entirely burst, and as soon as it bursts. If you see that it has burst, take hold of one of the bones in the ear, and burn the other until the thicker bone is as red as the junction; then do the rest of the bones until the acute is entirely burst, as we have said concerning the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the wisdom tooth, if it is of little bone, as like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great bone we must feel it, if it brings about the extraction of teeth; and that is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the worms in the ear, when you cure as we have said in the division and or treat with distillations, and the cure does not benefit, if you must know that the ear is exposed to the sun: if there are no worms to be seen, if the boils are small, and if they are not seen, take tweezers of this kind:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And so be careful and wide in the opening. And as for the most subtle chief of the ear according to the quantity of the patient’s suffering, then follow with all the antidote; do this often until you see it issue. And if it does not obey to issue, if I push around the cotton around the ear as I said at the stone; and if it still does not issue, if we have said, give distillations which the ancients have proved useful in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, in this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And so be careful and wide in the opening. And as for the most subtle chief of the ear according to the quantity of the patient’s suffering, then follow with all the antidote; do this often until you see it issue. And if it does not obey to issue, if I push around the cotton around the ear as I said at the stone; and if it still does not issue, if we have said, give distillations which the ancients have proved useful in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, in this way: Let silver or lead be split into small pieces, and above put on distillations; and pressing from these instruments, let there be a raiser and encircle the point immediately with cotton; then pour out your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the can; and let the can be in the ear; then press from the raiser all around the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or almost until the ear is emptied; and let the patient feel within, and let the distillations be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	And so be careful and wide in the opening. And as for the most subtle chief of the ear according to the quantity of the patient’s suffering, then follow with all the antidote; do this often until you see it issue. And if it does not obey to issue, if I push around the cotton around the ear as I said at the stone; and if it still does not issue, if we have said, give distillations which the ancients have proved useful in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, in this way: Let silver or lead be split into small pieces, and above put on distillations; and pressing from these instruments, let there be a raiser and encircle the point immediately with cotton; then pour out your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the can; and let the can be in the ear; then press from the raiser all around the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or almost until the ear is emptied; and let the patient feel within, and let the distillations be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same thing happens as adults with wounds or earwax that has become impacted. Such impacts never depart without leaving a mark on the ear, if we are not able to see them; and never happens without some loss of hearing, which we see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When such impact departs without being seen, it is a sign of serious disease in many cases, and in this case it is seen that you put the painful ear into the sunlight; look inside: if you see pus dripping, if the wound has all the pus, this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so be attentive both front and back all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the pus is of earwax or a piece of the ear, if you see small teeth and the lump is lighter, as much as the bone is whole.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if swelling is found in the ear, take one fine needle and lance a small hole at the fire, then insert the earlobe. If you feel the swelling which the patient feels at the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not break the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a plug according to the size of the hole, and fill in the cavity Egyptian style.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything until the wound is healed, or take a sponge soaked in rose-water and powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear flee, it is likely that you have pulled out the plug and put in another sponge soaked in oil of rose and wax until the swelling subsides.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If there is discharge of blood, soak a sponge and cover with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that will staunch the bleeding which are either to apply distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of paper scrolls.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Thus comes the paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry, if you extend them with thumbs and nails, and grasp with the tip of a spatula from their roots; then withdraw the vitreous body bruised
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you do not take care, if you burn with the lenticular cautery, after the incision it is worth moving; and often it breaks, so that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, their roots are scorched and do not come back anymore
de la gresle	Of the scab.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come on paper writings of blood things that seem to swell in their form and in their duration; and for this reason this disease is called "granulin", and is an assembly of great moisture in the marrow below and above; the work is like this: take hold of the limb if the granulin moves from one side to the other, and this is a light matter to know; then make a generous incision, then remove the marrow partly lightly, then take hold of the wound, and close. If you do not close it in the right direction you will not see blood in the wound; and if the wound is large, if the assembly has a cast, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for the marrow will restore itself quickly and leave behind pus.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulin descends downwards towards the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the limb, and extend the granulin with one grasp, and close and press from one side to the other; and if the tissue is loosened by the incision, this will cause no harm; and when the granulin is closed, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the limb of what is left behind until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	The oily exudate is enclosed in paper towels and this has happened more often to women than to men, and grief fills their eyes; they weep at dawn and dare not look at the sunlight because the tears hurry from their eyes; and because they lie with their faces down and sleep on their stomachs, and their paper towels are soaked with moisture that swells and causes them to appear covered in oily exudate. And when you press their limbs they feel the exudate between their toes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient puts his head in his sound health; then take one linen cloth and make a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of oily exudate from the chest part, and put it on; and press on the thumbs from one side and the other, so that the exudate is assembled together like the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture a trench with a wide incision, and let it not be more extensive than the wound made to the vein; and make the leather tough as long as you see the exudate; and in various situations comes exudate from the incision, according to the shape of a white fatty piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out all the fatty tissue between your thumbs at the back of your hands, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not put anything into the incision, until you have reached the oil, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it escapes not at the beginning of the incision, if you widen the incision slightly as much as it opens; then extract it as we have said, and moisten the bandage in oil and water, and put on the limb, and bind tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such fools who break their bones and put on por to corrupt that moisture which is gone. Then cure it until it is healed. And if it comes to the limb at the abscess, if you cure abscesses that are swelling so much that they are healed.
des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like substances grow hairs, adjust them other than their natural state, and are thickened, if they prick the eyes, they cause tears like customary tears and soften the papers and mucus, up to the point of destroying the eyes; the cure for this is threefold: either by entire fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside the cautery, or it is made by incision and suture or by strings, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s head in your left hand, then draw the paper from its root; if it is straightened, it is good; if not, if there is a splinter at any point of the root, either cut off the margin of the paper or the hairs will be torn out; and take one thread at the base of the paper and draw it to the tip; then stretch in the lower part of the paper, remove the hairs that have been adjusted, over the whole area, from the large tear until the small; then draw out one thread and place on the paper a small patch of cotton and bandage, then mark on the paper a sign like the spur of a myrtle, and it is known that the sign should be according to the quantity you see that the paper that is destined for you has been elevated.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if part that has to be treated has received a great quantity of paper according to what is known, then make at the whole of the area over the two lines that you have marked, and from the large tear until the small; and either the split is close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then take away the ointment from one of the two angles of the wound, then stretch; then gather the two layers with a suture of a needle with a thread of fine wool, and wipe off the blood, and do away with the surplus of threads on the two sockets to all things that stick to each other, as you see that it must be done; and if you do not see that it must be done, then leave the suture and the threads for two or three days; then cure the wound with a bandage of dry and constrictive things, because the paper will be healed at the bottom of the wound and the gathering of the two layers, but the suture is useless (as they say the old ones), and it is useful only in case of doubt.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: if you mark the mark of a figure which is just like the fuelle of a myrtle, as we have recounted, then in this case you must evacuate two onchons in accordance with the shape which is like this:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then grasp what covers it with small forces equally according to the shape which is like this:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pins, and the thing is not even, if you take a needle or there is a thread, and you tie it to the mark; and you take another thread and tie the great loop, and the second thread you tie the little loop, and you assemble between your two the threads equally; then keep your hand equally, and keep all the skin above where you have marked, as we have recounted, then assemble the two layers of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if there is an abscess at your incision, if you apply cerate and some soft dressings to soothe.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hairs of the beard have been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard and hair downwards as I have said, then make three incisions by art, and three threads as long as the beard and expand with mustard seed; and put in three hairs or hold the threads. Then assemble the one and the other securely above what is covered by beard oil, and strain the three hairs of the three parts. Leave it like that for several days, and the skin which has been strained will become black and dry and will fall out, as long as it persists.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and when the beard has fallen out, the hair will no longer prick; and this is the form of the three incisions that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a needle with its subtle thread; and there is.i. a silken thread which is subtle; then join the heads together and do not leave one and the other subtle, and let the length of the threads be equal; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not leave the chief of the thread; then put the patient's head in its place; and let the sun go if the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and minor work; then draw out the needle throughout the chase at the root of the hair in the armpit, and make it pierce in the paper hastily as much as you can; then draw out the hair until it is at the chase, and bring back to the chase that hair, if there is.i. or .ij. or .iij. or more; then draw out your hand until the vein comes out throughout the chase in the paper with the natural movement.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from the hole and you see it by the sight of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has grown back in its place and the wound has healed.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the festering comes to light, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.  And it arises from a wound, or from a bite or from cautery, and from similar things.
