Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way of working in this is that you make that suture, dry the layers, put in linen bands, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything else except for things that dry and restrain. For if you do that, if the disease comes back worse than before; but there must be softening things, like fennel; and vinegar or salt and linseed seeds boiled, and melted beeswax, and it should cover a bandage, and cure it in this way.</start_of_turn>
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must keep guard that it does not heal in a different form than before; and these works that we have mentioned are not fierce but only with regard to this disease, that it does not return in a different form than before.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the wound that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This ailment which is sored which truly is called 'axacrati', is natural and accidental. The accident arises from wound and cut and cautery and things similar; and the way of this work is that if you take an awl, in which there is a double thread, and the thread in the wound, and it makes split the left tear so that the thread of the vein is in two pieces; then the wound is at the bottom of all the awls, and the head is with one spatulate wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a scraper and put it in the wound, and rotate the swelling, and make two incisions or cut through the swelling; and if there are two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you have made, or make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as it is of a letter that has not 'j. grieche'; then break that bone, according to the quantity of its cost and swelling, of what teaches the swelling, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure that which we have said of the mollifying medicines and bands, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is recommended that you make a full incision over the hairs of paper; and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the learned doctors appear to know everything from great poverty to great wealth as to how to restore the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done of the work and the instruments in many situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the disease comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is recommended that you make a full incision over the hairs of paper; and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the learned doctors appear to know everything from great poverty to great wealth as to how to restore the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done of the work and the instruments in many situations.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling arises at home in a part as delicate as the nail of the thumb is soothed with oil, and cannot move or perform its natural works, if it is recommended that you should bathe the tip of a scraper over the swelling, and hold it high up; and extend as many times as necessary, until you have reached the point where the pain is neither too great nor too slight, so that the patient can endure neither too much pressure nor too little; and that your incision, which you will make to reassemble, be light, so that the nail returns to its natural shape; and all the reassembled parts must be thoroughly cleansed, and no longer bathed in salt-laden water, but in fresh water, and oil; and between the nail and the oil place a layer of linen, and cover with oiled wool in abundance; and afterwards apply poultices and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nails of the oil are two kinds: one is nervinous and seems like hard paste, and the other is not nervinous but seems like white moisture frozen; when one touches them with iron and boils them, they do not burn; both seem to commence towards the great marrow, and cross so much that they cover the whole cavity, light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his hand in his side, then opens the wound; and keep the hand at your side, then grasp the nail with pincers of little double curvature, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of sheep, or of beef, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and fix it in the nail, and pierce through the whole needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and wash away to the outside of the nail all the surrounding tissue that encompasses the nail and the hair to the hair, and leave the natural fat or marrow, if there are no tears usually from the incision; and in no case is the nail stretched only with the incision and the thread, as we have said; then it is washed with all the surrounding fat so that it is like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fatty tissue and break it, and that the needle is not perceived; and after the incision pour in oil a little ball of bruised silk, and put on a collar of litarge, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is left until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail of medicine is cured; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if the patient is feverish, take the spatula slightly blunt as in this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail superficially, and if you see that it has diminished point and the bone is pressed, if the liquid distills from your mouth into the oil collar of litarge and red ligature and bruised silk, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other work as before, until it is entirely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders thee in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk, and first cure the abscess with fire until it is healed, and then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if there appears cartilage softened at night in the oil by great discomfort, if you suspend it to the bone, cut off a part and not all, that blood does not arise; then distill in the oil of colera red which is made of litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes from the navel.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men never bear any mark of shame, and cover the pupil and bind upon papers and roll towards the flame; and seem like a rosebud. And if the patient puts his head in his bosom, the eyes vanish, and behold all that colour has a reasonable unity to that which is above, and supports it with force; then grasp the first colour, and go on grasping until the end, and keep only that which is left of the oil at the work. And let the incision be as slight as possible, as we have said in the incision of the vein, and have little force to hold the bone loose, as it is shown after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	When the incision is complete and the colour has been grasped, if you use oil of poppies or you distill collyrium red and similar corrosive medicines, put on the oil a cotton swab with an egg white, so that it is well secured; and if it does not move, and the patient has a suspicion of its being burnt, if you leave the oil and treat the burn with soothing things. Then return to your work until it is healed, and do as many colours as were ejected into the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But always know that you must nourish the cure of each feeble oil of the natural way; and in the work of fire; and do not stain your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	des voines des eulz
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	From the veins of the eyes
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two veins by degrees in one limb according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, if there is still blood remaining, distill in the oily coliere green and red to corrupt what is remaining doubtful.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot securely hold everything in that hour, make a plaster over the oil of calming things to soothe the pain of the eyes; and leave it until the pain is calmed and is assured to be free from post-operative swelling; then resume in the manner mentioned above until it is healed; and that is the form of the forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	If you cannot securely hold everything in that hour, make a plaster over the oil of calming things to soothe the pain of the eyes; and leave it until the pain is calmed and is assured to be free from post-operative swelling; then resume in the manner mentioned above until it is healed; and that is the form of the forces.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If you cannot securely hold everything in that hour, make a plaster over the oil of calming things to soothe the pain of the eyes; and leave it until the pain is calmed and is assured to be free from post-operative swelling; then resume in the manner mentioned above until it is healed; and that is the form of the forces.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is fractured, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the limb has all the instruments to be thus; it is called an "aspre chief," and is made of soft bone, like a chief rent, and is pointed as with a lime as when it is in this form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place over the limb the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two thumbs, and press your hand until you feel that the corruption is gone; do this never, and then restore the limb of exiccative medicines.</start_of_turn>
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And if the limb is swollen, and the marrow has not yet burst, and the bone of the bow is swollen, and remains so for eighty days, and does not recover and is not to be opened, and accidents happen thereby; know that it is sane; if not, if there is no other remedy than to restore the fistula to its natural position following this form: uncover the bone a second time by force, and by watery medicines, and when it is uncovered take hold of it following this form, and let the iron be at an angle of two right angles, and the bone be flattened until it is like this:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place your thumb on the bone below the elbow, and slip your hand away from the oil.i. immediately, then turn your palm upwards until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes out from under his hand if he keeps his hand on his elbow; and then restore the dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the thumb grows and persists, if there is matter at the elbow; if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the elbow, and slip your hand away from the oil immediately, then turn your palm upwards until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes out from under his hand if he keeps his hand on his elbow; and then restore the dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the thumb grows and persists, if there is matter at the elbow; if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the limb opens all around and there is no swelling or pain, if you suspect the patient; then grasp the limb, then apply a bandage or dressing to the wound and apply oil.i. mixed with acacia, aloe, incense and balsam, and strain the oil, and apply it over bandages and cloths; and keep the cloths in place if you take cloths that are soft enough, and double layers in three, and then put one over the other according to the quantity of wound there is between; then strain by means of a bandage stiff enough to form, and restart the dressings to suck the wound inwards; then hold the dressings and leave the oil strained out for night, and if the patient’s pain subsides, if you see the oil repair itself, that is good; if not; repeat the dressing and cloths and the limb and the dressings until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dou derrompement de toile uvee
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the dislocation comes in the armpit, then open, and comes out some papers like as many grains of resin; it is expected to see; then if you see it covered, the work is like biting a needle at the root of the lower part until the tip of it goes down, then put another needle there or there is double thread of the upper part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle in its place; then grasp the double thread and bind a part of the thumb together, and strain it well, then draw out the needle and put on linseed oil soaked in abundance of egg; and leave it as long as the thread is tight with the thumb, then cure the oil of comforting things until the wound is healed; and never is the wound restricted by the thumb nail part of a circle of wax, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound shows great appearance, if you pierce at the soft tissue which comes from behind and comes out with oil, correct the moist vaporous substance and draw out the wound, and put it back together; then draw it out as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the belly of the oil is swollen, it is not fire that causes it but the oil itself which is thick and sticky like descending water; and it is not so. The manner in which this swelling appears is as follows: if you make the patient sit upright and straight, then take hold of his head between your hands, and move it until you see the belly coming down to your eyes; then either bind it tightly or do not let the light go and see the patient do the things he used to do; and if it does not go down on its own, give it a pinch, for it is like water, and when it goes down again it does not appear as we have said. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the wound. That is, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corner of the wound and the crown, until the belly is gone. And when it comes out, distillate it in hot oil mixed with honey, or in vinegar or fenugreek boiled with honey, and then cure it with some other remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	When the belly of the oil is swollen, it is not fire that causes it but the oil itself which is thick and sticky like descending water; and it is not so. The manner in which this swelling appears is as follows: if you make the patient sit upright and straight, then take hold of his head between your hands, and move it until you see the belly coming down to your eyes; then either bind it tightly or do not let the light go and see the patient do the things he used to do; and if it does not go down on its own, give it a pinch, for it is like water, and when it goes down again it does not appear as we have said. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the wound. That is, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corner of the wound and the crown, until the belly is gone. And when it comes out, distillate it in hot oil mixed with honey, or in vinegar or fenugreek boiled with honey, and then cure it with some other remedy until it is healed.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis serre l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the water returns to the second passage, grasp the instrument with force and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, gently remove the almagda loop from around your hand and hand; then reintroduce the instrument into the water a little. Then pour from the vessel a little of the remaining oil. Then put on greasy cloths or toweling soaked in rose oil and a lot of eggs, and tie with the fragrant oil. Indeed, we and those who are with us will put on broiled meat with a lot of eggs on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the oil because there are pieces of bone that have too thick a hair, it is advisable that you take the instrument which is called the «alberit», for this is its shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And thus cut through the conjunctiva only, and do not linger too long, but make a small incision, then insert the needle, as we have said; and when the work is finished, appears to the patient a certain slumbering, in which he sleeps on his back in a single gloomy night; and let him be without any movement, and take nourishing foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and keep him still according to his disposition until three days; then take him home to the same gloomy night, and let him look around, and let him see nothing, and then restore him to his bed until the seventh day; and do not let him do anything else except for this cure or incision which is now being made, but let him be careful, for the pain will grow very great.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And thus cut through the conjunctiva only, and do not linger too long, but make a small incision, then insert the needle, as we have said; and when the work is finished, appears to the patient a certain slumbering, in which he sleeps on his back in a single gloomy night; and let him be without any movement, and take nourishing foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and keep him still according to his disposition until three days; then take him home to the same gloomy night, and let him look around, and let him see nothing, and then restore him to his bed until the seventh day; and do not let him do anything else except for this cure or incision which is now being made, but let him be careful, for the pain will grow very great. Leave the oil in front of the seventh day and address it to what soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, remove the dressing and put on his face a little ointment to cover any scabs, and keep it in that gloomy night. Then go out of the house and back in, and convert into his case; and his wounds that no disciple must interfere with in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Yrach who said that in sleep he had often seen a great light appear, as if by chance, but never had anyone seen it in our land, nor had I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of an almond, for he who does not know them will not know their way; and they are like peas in their pods:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their tops are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like an egg
de la char sor le neis	egg of the pear from the stone.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes births or deaths of various hairs occur, for there are some that appear like scorpions with teeth; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with blood colour, or if there is hairy swelling of bone colour. In this case of those hairs which is swelling, and is not entangled, it is to be known that you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and uncover his nose, and let the blood drain from those hairs, and draw out the nails; then press what you have put under the thumb of the subtle gut with one hand, until you are sure that that hair is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the vein has burst completely with delicate instruments, if nothing remains; and if without you sleeping or incisions are delayed, if support is needed as it should be; and if it is a malignant incision, hasten and cauterize as much as possible until the blood vessel is no longer stained and all the clots are gone. Then spit out or remove the blood clot easily and quickly with vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the blood does not clot, and moisture comes up to the palate, clots which are not bleeding; if moisture does not pierce as it should, clots which are in the marrow of the bone below, behold, the instruments do not come out whole: therefore it is necessary that you drink a thick thread of linen, and that you grasp our hands, and that there be no space between thumb and index finger; and put the patient’s arm in the palm of your hand at the shoulder, and press down until it comes out through the mouth; and do this smelling until it comes out through the mouth; and many times do this to the child as they have seen done; and it is a light thing for one who has seen it done; then hold the chief that comes out through the hand with one hand, and the other chief that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and pull out the clot alternately while holding our hands together; do this until you are sure that the clot has not been corrupted; then draw out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian unguents, and put it back in place as before; do this for two days or more, until the blood has clotted throughout; and then put in or remove a cautery once or twice a day until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them if necessary; this is the form of the instrument for purging the chief, from which we distill oils and medicines or blood.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of gold, resembling an overblown lamp, if like a chain, and guide it thus; and if you see, make a closed chain, and let the instruments be flat for purging the chief; and have one hand on the chief to hold it when we burn the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint to the elbow.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	From the shoulder to the elbow often arises a disease called "telul," which grows and becomes very large, to the extent that it is seen as an abnormal thing; and because of this it is commanded that you should begin by applying pressure at the start, and then break the bone, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in applying pressure until it is large, if you do not take precautions, it swells with blood, poor sense, and great pain: for if you touch it with iron, it is an inflamed abscess. For when it is once treated, if there is no blood swelling, you can see that you can easily control it; if the abscess is of soft touch, not of blood swelling, and you see that you can control it, you must evacuate the patient and control it in a timely manner, and treat the limb with drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the shoulder is cut and bound.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When solutions of continuation come into one of these cartillages of work, it proves useful, for in some homes. It is therefore necessary that this not happen to anyone, if one sees that the wound is fresh throughout its extent; and then one should raise the two thumbs to a splint, and cure until it is healed. And if the thumbs are already detached from one side and the other, one should hold all the parts of the thumb together until they bleed, and then assemble the two thumbs to a splint, and strain, and sprinkle with dragon's blood powder; and burn incense. And put upon the powder a piece of replacement of strength or another healing patch that binds, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the splint is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the belly splint; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the fractures of the thumbs
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, in the hands of the physician, are diverse wounds that resemble grains of barley, minor and greater; thus it is commanded to grasp the wound and make incisions around each hair, and grasp them with tweezers and pull them out from their root. Then apply pressure to the wound after the incision of the vitriol broth, until the bleeding has ceased. Finally, remove the dressing and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the root of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens that there is an abscess on the gums that the old people call "albulus"; if you support it, grasp the root and pull out the swelling or the blood; then put out the vitriol broth or other restraining and drying powders; and if the swelling returns after the incision, and happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; this is the shape of the instruments to carry out this work.</start_of_turn>
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	The teeth are never together at the root, between the gums, where the teeth are white and sharp; and never are the teeth black and yellow and toward, until the decay comes to the gum, and the teeth are biting; if you command that the patient sit between your hands, and their head be still, and open the teeth or the gums will burst, until nothing remains; and then you will make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as long as they remain; and if one breaks what is at the first root, that is good; if not, if you must repeat the second and third time, until you have everything back; and teeth that have had to move from various instruments to repair them, as this is what the work shows, for these teeth have other shapes than those that are between the teeth. And these shapes and others will appear to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you leave it too long without treating it, because one must not be ashamed to do so; for it is a material that is highly moist, therefore one has no excuse for neglecting it
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that the tooth is loose, many times the pain will depart from the patient, and care should be taken that it is neither too loose nor too tight; for otherwise it will not depart completely while the mischief is there. And when you are well certain that the tooth is loose, you must grasp the tooth firmly with all your might to ward off the jaw from all sides; then clench your fists with your two or three fingers and thumbs at the first and last points, as long as they are well extended; and then firmly fix the thumbs. Place the tip of the tooth between your knees and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, grasp the tooth straight forward with force, and if it does not budge, take no instruments and pull it out from the soft parts slightly, and move it as you did before. And if the root is perceived and broken, if you must fill it, you must cover it with bandages, either inside or outside; and if the painful tooth has been tightly held with clamps, do not break them while holding. It is necessary to moisten around the gum with sponges to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take great care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with the greatest pain of the first time. And take care that you do not make me do something like the ignorant layman, who by their haste and boldness break the harness every time, and do not bring me what we have told them; but bring me what often comes by the infection of this great disease from the roots that remain, or from the harness that they break, as we have often seen; and when the root is gone, wash the blood of wine or vinegar and salt; and if there is bleeding, as often happens, if you employ the juice of vitriol. And if that does not suffice, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of instruments, on which one must keep silence first, are either with long points and thick handles, that they do not double in number when you draw out the tooth; these are the shapes.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large limbs if they do not bend when drawing out, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so that one may hold them.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root comes loose when drawing out, if you must put out the moist cotton wool inside [i.e. gauze], as long as it is soft, then take away the clips which are called “algefri,” for in this way the head of the shoulder appears like a beak of a bird; and they must be made as with a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to withstand all these tensions, if you must uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place the instrument which is called «althali», namely tweezers, so that this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it must be forced and large so that it does not break, and if the root leaps by this means, that is good; if not, if you aid with all your instruments, so that the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has teeth, so that this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before the teeth, and this instrument that seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before the teeth, and this instrument that seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this; or that its force is such that it cannot break, and its jaws like those of instruments for teeth; and like other instruments which are not mentioned here; the master surgeon will find himself alone with his instrument, according to what his work and his illness show, for there are many diseases for which no instrument is taught in former times; and if it breaks not from bone or from any other part, or if it is necessary, if it seeks other instruments, as I have said, and helps him with gestures, for whose form is like this.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone, that it escapes not, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine that is convenient for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, and it is small, if the disease has passed with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear contrary to their natural course, and the shape is deformed, even among women of gentle birth, if it is suspected that the tooth is deeply lodged and cannot emerge naturally, and is not properly aligned, it cannot be soothed or comforted: therefore, extract it. And if it is close to the tooth, take hold of this instrument which is like a small beak, and which is made of iron without a sharp edge at the base:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hold it there with the thumbs and palms of your hands for the duration of the extraction, and because of that do not move the others, and if it appears, you can limber it, if you file a piece of file like this which is the shape of it.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is like filing nails; and while holding the tooth firmly with the thumbs and palms of your hands, slightly move the instrument to and fro, so that it does not move too much, and when you finish, leave no burr, for if the tooth is too deeply lodged and it bleeds the tongue, you must remove the sharp edges as much as possible so that it does not bleed the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth is loose, or by percussion or by biting, and the patient cannot press on that which sustains it except by biting, and you must cure it with restrictive medicines, which is not of use; if you must restrict it with a golden thread, for the silver thread becomes green and is harmful, but the gum does not move at all; and whether the thread is thick or thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, take the thread and double it between the two teeth in front, then place the teeth between the other teeth, if there are one or more, as long as you see it clearly until the sound tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering until you reach the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and cautiously, until it does not move; and if the thread is loose at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then grasp the teeth with tweezers and assemble them, and put them back between the sound tooth and put it in such a way that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it in place as tightly as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread. If it should remain and serve in this way, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two front teeth, and of the two back teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make the form of a tooth of a cow’s jaw, and put it back in its place or where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and hold and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper, lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	When the tongue hangs limp or is disordered by nature, or through an accidental wound; the work is such that you must cover the patient’s mouth with your hand and hold their tongue; then grasp the large nerve below the tongue, until the tongue is loosened from its place. If it persists or fails to yield, and this is the result of a wound, if you must uncover the wound, grasp the large vessel below; and when you have done this, if the bleeding stops easily and without difficulty, or with cold blood, then withdraw the tongue gradually, and keep the patient quiet until the bleeding stops. If blood spurts again, if necessary, withdraw the cautery and burn the vitriol at the tip; if this does not suffice, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is suitable for this; then treat the wound further until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see pus of a color or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a abscess; and if it is declining and there is moisture, if it spurts blood, grasp the cautery with a sponge and deliver from both parts; and if it does not stop your work, if necessary, apply a piece of vitriol to the tip until it is blackened, then return to your work until you have completed your procedure; then raise the limb easily and gently, and treat the wound further until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	The abscesses of the throat.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	The abscesses of the throat.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with tweezers, know that this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with tweezers, know that this is its form: grasp one claw at a time; when you have grasped one claw, grasp the other in the same way, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm, bitter, and soothing liquid; when blood spurts out, if there are pomegranate seeds or myrtle berries or similar things in the vomit, until the stain is gone; then wash the wound until it is healed. Never again shall there be any other incisions in the throat except for the two claws, if you grasp them as they are always grasped.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with a small abscess in her throat; that is to say, an abscess of little size; and I had her hold her throat very close, so that she could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and she died because she fainted from this. The abscess was so high that it had forced out two nails from the two holes that did not want to go in. I therefore took hold of both nails, and put one in each hole, and I pushed with great force; then I removed the other half in the other hole that did not want to go in, and I closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I put back the ointment in those abscesses, and I closed one half, and only a little blood escaped; and when I had finished, I extracted the passage from the throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, and she stopped fainting from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess reappeared in its place, filling her whole body that I had evacuated of food; so I grasped it again and cauterized it inside the throat: this time it went in a straight line; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened to her after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve, le feu ne doit être appliqué que quand les poils sont longs et égaux; et si l’on le pique à la racine, garder les yeux ferme jusqu’à ce qu’ils ne flottent plus.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	From the navel, fire should only be applied when the hair is long and even; and if it is pricked at the root, keep the eyes closed until they cease to move
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have put on a bandage or something to put the medicine on, if like the hairs of a sickle, put the instrument over the medicine on the navel; and the patient must rest on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth from the medicine inwards, if it does not reach the throat, and the hiccup; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the navel, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it wrinkled and the medications of the medicine are appeased; and if you see that, take hold and cover with any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and remove the instrument from the wound as much as the cotton fills it; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry and wipe off after three or five days. And if you must renew the cautery of the medicine, if you renew it, and after the cautery wipe off the surrounding with cotton wool, and pack what is around the medicine; and rise up cold water, and be cured of hiccups until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is more effective than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this manner. Take calamine and isops and origanum and rue and chamomile and avron and similar herbs. Assemble all or some of them in one pot, put in oil, and boil. Make sure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and put in one instrument that has a handle according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	This treatment is more effective than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this method. Take calamine and isops and origanum and rue and chamomile and avron and similar herbs. Assemble all or some of them in one pot, put in oil, and boil. Make sure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and put in one instrument that has a handle according to this method:
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened at the throat bone or fish spine, or nothing at all; if you therefore suspect that you see something, press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and remains in the throat, you must make the patient vomit the morbid; for by chance if it comes out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or some hardened bread; and tie the sponge to one thread, and then transfix it. And when it comes back, if it is swollen, then draw it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take one instrument of sponge according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the instrument is bent at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily and the head is raised up; keep your hands away from the epiglottis, for if you touch it, you will lose consciousness; do not press too hard on the bone inwards; and move the instrument only as much as necessary, for if the patient coughs or the thing is reversed, it will be all the same.
de la sansue de la gorge	If the instrument is bent at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily and the head is raised up; keep your hands away from the epiglottis, for if you touch it, you will lose consciousness; do not press too hard on the bone inwards; and move the instrument only as much as necessary, for if the patient coughs or the thing is reversed, it will be all the same.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	If the instrument is bent at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily and the head is raised up; keep your hands away from the epiglottis, for if you touch it, you will lose consciousness; do not press too hard on the bone inwards; and move the instrument only as much as necessary, for if the patient coughs or the thing is reversed, it will be all the same.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.
