Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	If she does not yield as we have said, if you submerge the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will have its effect. The method of fumigation is as follows: take a pot or one with charcoal inside, cover it with a gauze coverlet about a span wide, and make an opening in the middle through which the instrument will pass; then pour the fumigation onto the patient, and let the patient put their head into the can and close their mouth, so that the fumes do not escape but rise up to the nose; and the nose will now be affected, and if it does not yield, repeat the fumigation many times; and make the patient drink strong drinks, eat dirty and foul things, and refrain from drinking water; and thus it will come to pass that she will be forced by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument is thus that which we mentioned in treating the nose, if indeed it can be seen, resembles a pair of hooked tongs to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak of a rooster, and has lime-peel, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and thus is the form
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The wounds of the apostemes are, as it is remembered from one to the other in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways that they are produced. Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture covers the wound, color it as I have said of other abscesses.</start_of_turn
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introduction of the medicine there comes no moisture, if it is fat, if the former has gone in a cross, and takes hold as hooks, and scorches lightly from the side and holds the coat where you grasp it with the thumb;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If you do not grasp it firmly, if you tear it piecemeal, then nothing will remain.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, if it returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it lingers for a moment, without causing you concern, if you apply to the wound some corrosive powders, hold the wound steady, and put upon it soothing things around the circumference; and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.

If the vein swells up against you or another if you are hasty and use broken vitriol, and leave it for one or two days, until the wound has healed, and rest the swelling of blood; then return to the cover that was removed when it was dislodged
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the entromittent instruments, and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are four squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, for enclosing fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are like the needles which we use to ligate wounds, and they are of citrine, or iron, or silver, and the thread is yellow, and they are better at closing black wounds for enclosing fistulas.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of lice are like those of seeds, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and if lice have twice the curves of two hands, they are just as numerous.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of lice are like those of seeds, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and if lice have twice the curves of two hands, they are just as numerous. And if lice have two curves and are of two hands; or if lice have one curve only and are of two hands; all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these lice is very sharp, and there are some that do not pierce but one side only, of which we must be careful, because they do not cut through flesh but the bone.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And among these interjections are the elements that are restored in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them during the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	One should use them only in bone fractures, such as legs, arms, arms of the shoulder, and ribs, and in similar cases.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And never make any other small instrument, resembling the nails of fists, according to this form, as we stop blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And put it nowhere near blood vessels or arteries, never again in the same form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never swell the breasts of women when they begin to decay, as they seem like breasts of a female;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain still, weeping and fleeing, and whoever sees them cured must believe that they must be treated in this manner from the beginning until the end of this line b until .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and use the medical plaster to cover the wound, and then gather the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and cure until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the breast leans forward and is eased by its greatness as when women have it, if the force be in two ribs below, by two similar fissures;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	or that one holds the other at the end of both, so that the greater line contains the less according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin between the two ribs, and remove the fat, and mix in what we have said of stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healthy, or the incision is not quite finished, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the discharge of blood, if it is necessary, that you fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive order.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it has consumed the remnant and the fat, then cure it when it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	And leave it until it has consumed the remnant and the fat, then cure it when it is healed.

Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	And leave it until it has consumed the remnant and the fat, then cure it when it is healed.

And when all the hair in the abscess is drained, if the wound is of great extent, fill the wound with fine cotton, and leave it until the other side, then extract all the cotton, and cure the swelling that arises from this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant. de la routure de l’artere	of the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is blocked, and the skin above is swollen, if there are many abscesses there, there will also be escape of blood from the vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the wound is left open as long as the artery is blocked, if there are abscesses at the root of the vein they will grow long and burst.</start_of_turn>
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it, if you feel it is a loosening; and when it is the vein, there will be running away of blood from the wound.</start_of_turn
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	it is foolish to close this wound, and even when it is soaked in blood the abscesses and wounds and boils and other things will grow large.

puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then support the limb with a needle, and pierce it through to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread as I have taught you concerning the extraction of the veins in the temples;

et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the swelling is as big as the belly, if you must, hold your hand over the abscess from the very beginning.</start_of_turn>

des apostemes des ners	Des apostemes des ners.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	The abscesses come from the nerves as well as from the veins, as from the nerves when they are cut or overworked, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens with wounds and tumours, or with joints, and it is that there is excessive swelling, and its colour resembles that of dark yellow, and is in many cases accompanied by pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is pressed, if it causes pain, and is not easily pierced by the point of the thumb, but is accompanied by swelling;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And he must remain still from every side, neither forward nor backward, neither to the left nor to the right, neither from above nor from below; and he who is in joints must not be covered with iron: by chance it may cause contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is at the head or shoulder or chest, must make the skin taut over the bone.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the swelling is small, if the limb has a tension, and you press it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is great, if the swelling has become soft, and it is bruised, then you must break it up and unite the wound at the suture, and keep it healed until it is well.
des grosses boces pendans	From the armpits hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	From the armpits hanging there is often in the belly and not elsewhere that this ailment exists, and is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to nails, and its root is subtle, and its head is large; and there are small and great ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen two homes where out of a hundred there were two or more bellies which appeared more like nails than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were split open, and cured by moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them out and found in one sixteen-and-a-half ounces and in the other fifteen and three-quarters, and the work in the incision is such that if you look you will see that the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist and has a thick root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. For in this case, there often comes excessive bleeding, and if it does not stop, do not delay but immediately perform the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient groaning and pale from the incision of the wound, take a piece of well-made sponge, bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for three days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	Then the restraint, and do not stop constricting the sponge until the artery is ligated; and if the roots are large, if there is pain in the belly, but do cover half of the wound well,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then let the cautery be performed so that it does not recoil; then cure the wound and keep only the hair that is of a coarse colour and poor sense and milk-white.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	When the abscess is full.</start_of_turn
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	When there appears a swelling, it comes from a burn or incision of the flesh, and is above the belly and there are some pus there, as in other ways, or blood which clots blood vessels or arteries according to what is in front, or swelling;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If by fistula or passage of the bowel, if it is the color of the abscess, it is a slight thing causing pain, and there are various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If by passage of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when it is pressed, it returns, and by chance if it is choked, and expands the mouth at the entrance of the bath and with great effort.</start_of_turn>

dou chancre	Then strain the abscess for three days on the needles; if you see it, pierce the needles, and leave the wound open until it bursts, and remove the dead tissue by itself.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have already mentioned the signs of an abscess, and how it should be treated with medicine and how to shun the cautery; and we say that an abscess swells in the marrow, and has great swelling in the cure. The ancients say that when an abscess is in the flesh or can be scraped out as when an abscess is in the marrow, in the spleen, and in similar places, it must be removed as soon as possible; and when it is large and old, if it cannot be cured, do not approach it, for I know of no cure for it. No one has ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And as for the work, when it is in the flesh or can be removed, as we have said, do not purge the black bile from the patient once; then make the patient healthy if there is still any swelling left; then expel the patient, i.e. give him a good drink to make the work; then draw out your needles or abscesses, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb at your hand or at nothing, and if the wound becomes infected from the incision of the artery or vein, do not cauterize too much lest it be stained; then cure with another cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already spoken concerning the resemblances of hydrophobia, and that when an assembly of water is made, signs of jaundice resemble; the cure which is made by medicines and that which is cured by iron: if only the lightning is alight; and one must not touch iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and icterus, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore when medicines are given for this semblance which is called "lightning" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if one observes that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides hydrophobia, as with all solutions of the stomach and similar things; if one does not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if one sees the patient of great strength, and there is no other disease besides hydrophobia alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, one must operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	We have already spoken concerning the resemblances of hydrophobia, and that when an assembly of water is made, signs of jaundice resemble; the cure which is made by medicines and that which is cured by iron: if only the lightning is alight; and one must not touch iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and icterus, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore when medicines are given for this semblance which is called "lightning" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if one observes that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides hydrophobia, as with all solutions of the stomach and similar things; if one does not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if one sees the patient of great strength, and there is no other disease besides hydrophobia alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, one must operate:
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	We have already spoken concerning the resemblances of hydrophobia, and that when an assembly of water is made, signs of jaundice resemble; the cure which is made by medicines and that which is cured by iron: if only the lightning is alight; and one must not touch iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and icterus, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore when medicines are given for this semblance which is called "lightning" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if one observes that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides hydrophobia, as with all solutions of the stomach and similar things; if one does not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if one sees the patient of great strength, and there is no other disease besides hydrophobia alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, one must operate:
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce through the leather with the instrument, and grasp it, and keep your hand all the way up between the leather and the bone as though you were escorting the amount of an nail or something similar; then pierce the bone until the space comes up to the tip of the tooth, that is the limit of the pain, then pull out the instrument, and behold, that is the shape of this instrument: It is like a slender silver needle, and is made of steel or silver wire, and has at the bottom a small hole; or costs one, two holes; and three on one side, and one on the other. And the head of the instrument is cut off like a pen, and that is the shape of the incision which the writers make for the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top of all this is the ailment, so that when the instruments are put to the test, if now at the same time that they are put to the test; empty out then half or a third part, for if you empty out more than that which is proper for this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will bleed profusely, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty out according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the provisions of the virtue for the patient signify, and his pains; then draw out the instrument and retain the blood, and it is retained now by the knot which I have mentioned that stamps the perforation which is on the bone, as I have said; pierce according to this manner; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering from that, and draw out a small quantity of blood.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do nothing of the sort; keep yourself from using it until it stops hurting. And if you are in doubt about the patient, and you insert too much water, if the cure be of burying or washing with sand, with water or bathing and in the sun, and abstain from eating; and let the physician give drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Do nothing of the sort; keep yourself from using it until it stops hurting. And if you are in doubt about the patient, and you insert too much water, if the cure be of burying or washing with sand, with water or bathing and in the sun, and abstain from eating; and let the physician give drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never is a child born without having a hole in the belly, or the hole is small, or it is not well placed. If the physician urges too much and has not pierced at all, despite great swelling, in this form: then put or pierce with a blunt needle of lead, and tie and hold for two or three days. And when he wants to urinate, if you leave the hole closed, he will urinate, and then you will restore him; and by chance you will not be able to do anything, for the urine that comes out will not leave the hole closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the opening is small, if medicine be applied with lead weights, as we have said, if it dilates. Those who have not the opening in their limb are black, for none are born who have the opening at the head of the bone, for they cannot urinate before they raise their thigh; and they cannot urinate effectually for that the matter cannot reach the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that if the patient lies recumbent on his back, then the head of the thigh and the knee are as large as a pen; if the opening is small, if it comes to a thousand, as it is convenient; and you must take care of the evacuation of blood which comes often, and if it comes, if the stain of that which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pus of the thigh.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these boils to the verge, and are an unsightly sight; and in them are both malignant and non-malignant things; if you take them at their face value, with ointment of subtlety, and press and squeeze them all out, then put on a wet bandage in the Egyptian fashion; then cure with diafinicon until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the boil is malignant, with pus-filled color and discharging, if you take it at its face value, you must bring cautery. When you have squeezed it, and if the boil is at the root of the verge, and some is inside the skin and some outside, if you must break the boil which is inside first; and when it is healed, if you cure the outside, if you do not secure the edge of the verge, blackening and corruption will come into the verge or around the wound; if you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then leave on the place of honey and flour which is made of pomegranate peel and sometimes, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	If blood comes out, if you bring lunar cautery in this form: the cautery helps with these two things: the evacuation of blood and the corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and retracted, if you drink or cause the verge to bleed a thumb of plum, and the patient urinate; and when the hair has been burned away from the head of the shoulder which has not been circumcised, or if there is wound or incision, if you must then burn the hair with a needle, as long as the hair is loosened, and deliver the hair from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	If this be a grievous matter, if you must certainly undertake it, then grasp the limb firmly without inflicting any wound to the root of the thumb and the heel; then gradually separate the skin between the two joints, and place a fine strip of moist linen over the cold water, so that it does not slip away.
de la circoncision	If this be a grievous matter, if you must certainly undertake it, then grasp the limb firmly without inflicting any wound to the root of the thumb and the heel; then gradually separate the skin between the two joints, and place a fine strip of moist linen over the cold water, so that it does not slip away.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of the other wounds; however, when our will commands it, and is properly undertaken, if it is necessary that our workers do the best work, and the most gentle for the patient.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old folks do not tell me of circumcision for their children, for they do not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and physicians who perform circumcision to make incisions around the head of the penis, and with force, and with great bleeding; so that the testicles often flee because of the two layers of skin, and by chance if one severs these below and leaves the upper one behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound closes again, and the pain is doubled, and there is swelling which is painful when the point of the limb is not securely held; and by swelling of the cord by chance escapes the wound, corrects the work, and many times comes out without having had to perform any swelling and I think so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the alteration which is made with force throughout the whole thread, I have observed the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if it is held equally on every side in this way, all the tension is equal; but if the thread is well twisted round the leather; and if the manner is like that of the first work, if you make the child think, if he understands, do not force him to tighten the thread too much around the limb, but rather let him join it in all the ways that you can
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then hold your hand straight out between your hands or from your toes that the child does not see them, neither any instruments; then take hold of your hand at the limb and breathe or cough, and pull it up as high as the head of the limb is bent; then mix well the ordure that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, and tie from this to that with another thread; and hold two by the second loop at the pouch and the thumb, and push between the two threads, then leave the thumb upwards until the head of the limb is well healed and pull the chief of the limb.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood flow freely, and freely; for it is the physician’s wisdom; and put powder on and about the powder. i.e. a bandage that adheres with an egg-shaped lump of gum, scraped from rose oil, confirmed with rosemary oil and balsam, and leave it on until the bleeding stops. And cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	When the forces are formed at the armpit, it is thus: the two arms are tense and stretched, and the arms are as great as the palm of the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the armpit is when the nerves are injured during the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your nail, even if it causes the wound to split; and grasp it equally, and if you do not manage to hold it with your nail, if you grasp it with your teeth, hold it firmly, and then grasp it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass for two days, and what is below the ribcage is inflamed, if you leave it as long as the spasms cease, and the swelling is slight; if you touch it as you wish, and hold on to the lower part of the ribcage, it will do you neither good nor harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have treated the wound with powder, as we have said or mentioned, if you touch it too hard, it will go deeper; so treat it as we have said until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	When the urine is retained.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is frequent in the cases of stone, or of blood clot, or of bile, or of worms, or of other things mentioned previously.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the stone is in the kidney or the neck of the bladder, then you must make the patient hunch over his knees; and put his feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part below his back, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine can flow freely.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “siringues”; and this is the form: either of hammered silver slightly curved like a dove; or the caine of a long and a half palm, or subtle at the head
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And thus the method of extracting urine is as follows: if you take one double thread and tie one end to a ball of wool or cotton, and pass the thread through the bladder; and drain the excess wool and stop at the top of the bladder, then join the bladder with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and the testicles with oil moist and oily with olive oil and tepid water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then insert the bladder gently into the vagina, until it reaches the root of the vagina; then double the vagina backwards towards the abdomen; then drain the bladder until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel it come out until it is empty; do this not otherwise than in this order, for otherwise it will conduct or go wrong; then tighten the thread at both ends, and the urine will follow the thread, and then remove the thread, and correct the urine
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the bladder until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are dropsy or blood in the bladder, or putrification has set in, and you see urine and medicines distilled, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it has a hole: two parts on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and you must support the bladder so that the medicine may be as effective as possible, if we can drain the moisture, and push out as much as possible.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see the medicines dripping from the bladder, put the chief of the bladder in the moisture, and push out the one that is causing the pain; if you push out the moisture from the wound, and then push back the one that is causing the pain; if the moisture enters the wound, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if it is like this:
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it round about; then stretch a strong thread through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a ball, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and bind it with the instrument; and do as you would if you had made a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the previous division the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction alongside medicines; and we have mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that must be extracted, as well as the signs and in what case a stone must be opened; in the bladder and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and briefly.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is retained in the bladder often causes vomiting, which is a sign that the stone has burst from the bladder similar to the pain in its subtlety; and it opens gravel, and grinds the patient’s side, and causes them to urinate frequently, and then it swells; and from these vomits the foundation is loosened; and the healing of these vomiting spells is light up until the age of three years, and is more grievous in the elderly, and is like that in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure for these who have a large stone is lighter than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a catharsis, to drive out all the worms that are in the intestines. For they obstruct no time the opening of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the limbs, and loosen and move to the outside, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not ever go too high up; then make him sit between your hands visible, and his hands are at his sides, so that the bladder is all the way down swallowing; then query and touch it then.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hurry now to cut on the stone. And if it does not bleed on touching with the whole hand, if the patient is fat, take your left index finger, if the patient is young and robust; and press on its foundation, and query the stone, and when you feel it with your thumb, if the bladder is inflamed; then press on your thumb, and the stone will come out whether you see it cut.</start_of_turn
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his thumb on his right hand and his little finger on his left hand the skin that is between the thumb and little finger in the part where the measure is taken; then insert the sponge, which is shaped like this.

par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if two thumbs which are or support, that it leaps forward in work; and the sponges that are in the part of the stone or where there are angles, and margins: if they are grasped to tighten; and if there is anything that is swollen, like a gland, and rounded, from which issue is slight.</start_of_turn
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles or margins, make the size greater; and if it does not slip, know that you must strain above the tenailles which are just like a file at the head, for must strain the stone if it does not escape; or you may use a curved instrument at the head. If you do not know how to handle it, it is wide; if it is blunt, it is a fracture of the glass.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the limb above and below, then push the bone sideways between the two joints, and then extract it with force, loosen the ligament, and congeal the blood that is in the wound; then cure as before.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is dislocated in a woman, and this does not happen often, it is a grievous cure, and is defended by two things: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who is truly virtuous, even among the most chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is if by chance one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth method is if the woman's stone is more blunt than the man's, for in that case one can make a deeper size, and greater fear has it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need this, if you take a woman who is very well-versed, and prick the root with a needle, and if you do not find it, not even a slight tremor; and present a woman who is wise in life, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command with the inquiry of the stone.

de hernie carnouse	of hernia of the abdomen.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is like lead when cold, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the coion between the white fat that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramiculus is weak and comes from the coions, and the matter is spread out
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the coions, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or pale blue, and this is more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of a dislocation of this limb, for if it is white or bluish like we have said, if the abscess is round like a ball and does not open, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and for this reason people think it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the limb and the bluish layer, if you feel well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it appears throughout the inside as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, following the introduction, judge what is within.

et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eye socket swells up during the operation, hold the eye in its place until you have finished the procedure; then join the two corners of the eye socket together with a suture, and cure it like any other wound until it has healed.</start_of_turn>

The wound must be enlarged, that is to say, the abscess must be drained, and it must be sutured after about twenty days or when the pain has subsided, and when it is sutured as before, the patient will be well again.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the incision of the hip bone
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Hair that is in the vicinity of this branch has doubt and fear in many places, for it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I will tell you about the work and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that abscesses come from boils or carbuncles, and sometimes from wounds; and this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive and sudden heat, which expands and bursts boils or carbuncles.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is the colour of the abscess according to the colour of urine; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess of grief.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And thus an abscess is grieved with fear and tears, of foul colour, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.</start_of_turn>
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the position of the abscess burn, when you press it on your shoulder;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	you must not touch it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	Whoever has made an incision in a vein is known by the way his fingers tremble at the touch of two.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can make the size of this kind and of others like it well enough;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you take care of the nails like nails of coions, then put the egghead in the air, and put out the yolk with white salve, and deliver the yolk from all its parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already cooked with these things, if you must, then only treat the egg and the nails.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is high up on the surface of the bone, or in the blood vessels, it is necessary to deliver all that is taut, and to round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the bone is high or behind the joint, if you must grasp it entirely, and draw out the head, as we have said.</start_of_turn>

When your work is done, if you are using wool yarn, soak it in rose oil and wine, then bandage it with other bandages until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the bones
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enveloped in a covering resembling a bladder, with the softening of the joints.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans in pain when he moves.</start_of_turn>
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is as perilous as this one before mentioned.</start_of_turn

et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and these events of this root are if it is by the section that comes or the extension above the belly in the part of the flanks, because the intestines descend from that route to one of the hips;  and these events can be caused in various ways: by percussion, or jumping, or pressure, or by lifting a burden, and in various other things;  </start_of_turn
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is a swelling of the face, if there are some and some, in long tension, and does not come immediately;

And the sign is when the face is sectioned, that it makes sudden pain appear at the edge, and the swelling is diverse in appearance, from the splitting of the skin to the bursting of the bowels, because of the evacuation of the intestine and the displacement of the bone from the face.</start_of_turn>

Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of fire with fear, for it is known to escape.

Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and the limb remains painful even after it has recovered; and if it is delayed in recovering, if it be from a hot bath, put on what we have mentioned above until it recovers;

de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the groin.

Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained and does not appear on the surface, and the cautery is muffled in this limb, and more proximate to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the nails of the thumbs are softened in water-soaked homes, because the nails that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when you see it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to scrape off the softened skin from the natural skin; then join the layers together with a suture, and if you see that, close the superfluous softened skin with two or three sutures firmly; then scrape between the sutures, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the hair.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement,
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	When the shoulder is dislocated by moisture, and is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites are beings that possess both male and female sexual organs.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like that of women: one if between the two testicles is opened as with the nature of a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes in the urine they are emitted. And the other way if in women, and there is upon the navel like a beard and two testicles. And the cure of the swelling and the fame is if you cut out all the seminal vesicles, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a seminal vesicle above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand. And the cure is to hold it lightly with the hand or fingers, and do not move it too much, for there is danger of bleeding, and then the cure for other diseases is to be made as soon as possible; and there is another ailment that comes from the root of the kidney, and the pain, and by chance it leaps out, and is like the semblance of a cow, and for this reason it is called the ancient “sickly disease”. If you can remove it, as we have said concerning the tentigene, and cure it when it is well.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When the natural position of the woman is not clearly perceived, or if the passage has been too slight; or if it is by birth, or by disease that has come to pass; or if it is by an injury of the arm or a swelling or stiffness of the limb, and if it is caused by an infection of the armpits, or by worms or ulcers, or any other cause; and if the bruise or swelling is painful, and if the joint is inflamed, or if the limb is stiff, then it must be reset. If the swelling is slight and is close to the armpit, grasp the two thumbs and place the woman on her back, spread out her legs; then stretch out the two thumbs as much as the swelling of the armpit allows, and as long as the stiffness of the limb persists; then take hold of the limb, anoint it with oil, and place it on the limb, and keep the woman still for a moment, as if she were dead; if the swelling is hard and stiff, it must be forced out like a hazel leaf. If the swelling comes from a wound, if it is necessary to support the wound, grasp the heel of the wound with your thumb and index finger; and place the woman on her side, extend her legs; then the wound will stretch out as much as the swelling of the limb allows, and as long as the stiffness persists. Then take hold of the limb, anoint it with oil, and place it on the limb, and keep the woman still for a moment, as if she were dead. If the swelling is from a nail, if it must be grasped, support the swelling as described above. For in the armpit infection arises from the swelling of the armpit, do not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are openings of veins which, without treatment, are usually fatal. When emorroids are old, they become toughened. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms; here I will tell you of those which are most useful for curing. I say that emoroids and the toughened vein, when they are inflamed in the belly, are not felt unless they are treated by iron. Those which are at the root of the belly can be felt; these can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then draw the belly tight, grasp the root and sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water. If there is still pain, give her a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then give her barley meal with honey and assails, and make her drink it. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, make her breathe vinegar at her back and give her lead. Then give her lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with old wine, and make her breathe. And when the incision is healed, if it is a bleeding vein, it will stop bleeding as long as it is healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough chief, as I have already said of the toughened vein; and then it will stop bleeding as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Emorroids are openings of veins which, without treatment, are usually fatal. When emorroids are old, they become toughened. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms; here I will tell you of those which are most useful for curing. I say that emoroids and the toughened vein, when they are inflamed in the belly, are not felt unless they are treated by iron. Those which are at the root of the belly can be felt; these can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then draw the belly tight, grasp the root and sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water. If there is still pain, give her a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then give her barley meal with honey and assails, and make her drink it.
