As for bleeding from the belly, this must be treated by an opening at the root.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Emorroids are openings of veins which, without treatment, are usually fatal. When emorroids are old, they become toughened. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms; here I will tell you of those which are most useful for curing. I say that emoroids and the toughened vein, when they are inflamed in the belly, are not felt unless they are treated by iron. Those which are at the root of the belly can be felt; these can be cured. As for bleeding from the belly, this must be treated by an opening at the root of the belly. Many methods of stemming the bleeding of the belly have been mentioned; such as carbuncles, perforated abscesses, herpes, stomach ulcers, fistulas and emoroids, and infected wounds of the belly. It is therefore necessary that you keep the woman in a cold house, then draw the belly tight, grasp the root and sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water. If there is still pain, give her a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then give her barley meal with honey and assails, and make her drink it. And when the incision is healed, if it is a bleeding vein, it will stop bleeding as long as it is healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough chief, as I have already said of the toughened vein; and then it will stop bleeding as long as it is healthy.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy. The midwife first of all must know the figure of the natural birth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down on the jaw, and desire to smell the head: then the child is eager to be born; then the afterbirth follows which is according to the natural figure, and comes out with the head, and is supported by her; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on her belly, if the child comes out head first, he will be supported by her; for when he comes down on his head, he is supported by her, and is delivered of his superfluities by a natural movement; and this is not otherwise. For it does not come at any time from his feet, or from the hips or arms, or from his belly or buttocks, but is turned by an accident from his collar, and by other harmful figures; if the midwife is skilled in the art, she will be wise and discreet in these matters, and will avoid error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures that we must use to aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out head first by natural birth, and the woman is groaning, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and when she has given birth of the oile or fenugreek seed, then lie between her legs the little cushion which is its form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And split the second finger, and bind its nail until the moisture which is in its core flees; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with muscle of fennel with oil of sesame; then make her vomit and evacuate feces, and keep her mouth and nose covered for an hour: if the fetus is now gone. And if both hands go out violently, if you must, that you hold them gently and cautiously; and if they do not enter, if you put the woman on her seat, and keep her feet high; then withdraw the seat from the earth, and hold her, that she does not move; and if the hands do not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you bind the hands at the wrist which is before mentioned, and pull out the fetus, and calm her equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the issue of the fetus on his feet.

et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then the head of the shoulder must be turned back and forth, until it is even;

si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps up, God helps.

de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, if as I have said in the division, and he does not flee, and you are constrained by the work of your hands;

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman with a child in her womb who had a miscarriage, then consulted with another concerning it, and refuted the miscarriage of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came an abscess in the belly, which grew so large that it burst, and began to cause great swelling.</start_of_turn>
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went for help to the doctor, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the bleeding.</start_of_turn
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong dressing, and out came a bone, and after that a few days another.</start_of_turn>
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at you, for your belly has no bone.

Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, which is what we have learned from books; and two returns as two thumbs of two hands.

et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And in the midst let the two lips be doubled to the jaw, which are firm one against the other, half a palm in length or more.</start_of_turn>

et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And thus there are often six joints that are loosened, as you see, from a palm of length, and two of width;

Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very formidable, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one beholds them appear, the work hastens, and the higher one's home is for their quantity.

toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, whether cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put in a caustic or cut at the bottom of the pot, and the other at the mouth of the mare.

de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	When children are born who do not have their foundation firmly established, they are stamped with a subtle scab.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore you must drive the heel of the scab towards its root without causing further damage, and keep the opening closed so that it does not touch;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on soft linen soaked in wine and oil, and then the ointment until it is healed.

de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula at its root.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	those which arise from the foundation are nodular, and greater than those which arise from below the foundation, or between the two parts,

Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows if the fistula is closed at its base, and does not go deeper:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bite your thumb or foundation, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, if you insert a blunt attempt of sponge, or hair of a horse, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair on your thumb;

saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	The bandages must not be too tight; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula persists up to the bladder or the urine tube, if in leaping the urine escapes and cannot be retained by medicine.

s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the pain is not violent, if there is any swelling at all, neither medicine nor treatment by fomentation is of any use.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no other cure than toil, and the folly of the fools who interfere with them

si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not slip away immediately, it cannot be healed.</start_of_turn>

des emorroydes	bleeds.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	Injuries are of two kinds: when they are deep-seated, like grains of resin, and are small or large; or when they are close to the surface of the skin. And when there is one or more of them, they break the foundation and the top of the foundation; but those which are broken have much moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and are accompanied by an abscess or a yellowish fluid or blood, and have a yellow color.

Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont.

Formice is a small appearance that appears before the body, and goes out from within; and never does its true nature grieve, and is perceived as if dead, and comes into all the limbs, and more on the hands than any other part.

des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the previous chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and surgery, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on how they are made, and depending on the parts or wounds that are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the bite of a stone, and the size of a spear or nail, or of a lance or fist or spit or something similar;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	When the cause of the wound is known, as when a wound occurs on the neck, or the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, or similar parts of the body;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	When the cause of the wound is known, as when a wound occurs on the neck, or the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, or similar parts of the body, I shall tell you of the cure for a simple wound and begin with wounds of the head alone, for the memory will return in its chapter.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no cracking of bone or anything of the kind, and the skin is completely ruptured and the wound is large,  </start_of_turn

et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen carefully to the patient's swelling of wine and meat.

et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and take out the wound, if it is infected, cover the abscess with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine.

et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it has already moved, place over it some soft materials until it is healed.</start_of_turn>

dou derrompement dou ventre	But about the loosening of the belly...
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The loosening of the belly is great and middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From great wound comes no time for the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the introduction of worms.

et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and thus if the shoulder is dislocated downwards in one of the two parts.</start_of_turn>
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then let the upper part of the limb be higher than the lower.</start_of_turn>
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus I command you to do in wounds large and deep.</start_of_turn>
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds cause this that thou seest appearing.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then keep between your hands, pity the poor thing that holds all the way through its hand,
et assemble les levres;	and gather the limbs.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	that is the common method of stitching together.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	And take an awl or more, according to the quantity of the wound's size.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave some space around the wound, i.e. about the width of a thumb, and insert an awl or if there is a lot of flesh, a needle with strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two layers of skin with the two layers of fat,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is from the inside of the skin, until you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	et assemble les joints du chef du scapula les trois ensemble.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the strain of a doubled thread around the hook of three parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the three bones of the wound successively,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one space, and insert another hook;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then the thread should be as fine as the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing that until you have done as many needles as you have been told.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wounds are restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles be moderate, between soft and hard,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	For the subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and the too large ones if they do not enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be blunt.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and must not be forced too deeply into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	causing them to penetrate and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	Then hold the head of the pins of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while he sleeps.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths over the head of the pins of the needles to hold them,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	For there is often an awl or something sharp.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second costure is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and that you assemble the awls of leather and the awls of bone together with an awl or there is a strong thread between them;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	when you have pierced these things through all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you remember the needle at the part where you began, in the way that we commenced, it will cost you dearly.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put an interval between the stitches the thickness of a nut of a minor kind.</start_of_turn>
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch will hold the flesh.</start_of_turn
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound like this which has a hump or belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	Who was the owner of the knife?
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm wide
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were very well filled with great things,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I will restore the intestines when they have been out for .xxiiij. hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	The wound was sutured for .xv. days, and the patient recovered well.</start_of_turn>
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the madman thought he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not cure him of the wound, for I am in a place where there is no medicine, neither any remedies;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the method more effective for the wound is to put mustard plaster on nine times the size of the wound, and to bathe with a honey-infused liquid until it heals.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or thus I shall tell you the nine proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and pass it from the underside up to this depth;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the knot on the right side, if you let go of the needle, it will slip or wrinkle or you will have pushed the needle through,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	And the fire burns from the inside outwards until it escapes;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And understanding of this chapter is that if you do as a leatherworker does with the skin,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leaves once the hair from one side, and takes it back from the other, until the hair has grown completely.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of treatment is that of Galiens, which is done properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If it is so that no one does it, who can reassemble the injured parts naturally.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and join one of the ends to the other end, in a moderate way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or hook nearby, and pierce that part only,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the ends of the bone in place;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then draw the needle and make it pierce from the lower part until it reaches the cavity,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as indeed done with the scapula.</start_of_turn>

et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the common method of treatment and the most common.</start_of_turn>
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Foreign tongues are silent, and no witness bears,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	we must suture the belly with needles, or there is thread in the flesh;

Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The wound is judged as being as severe as any other wound.</start_of_turn>
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved,

Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot heal when they are swollen.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	It is because of the swelling of the veins and the brittleness of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gut leaps out of the wound, if it is reset backwards just as the intestine, while it is fresh;

de la routure dou boueil	except for the root of the boil.</start_of_turn

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head of the intestine is split, and there is no further nuisance to the patient,

Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule».

et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is just as chewed as the quill of a bird;

et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and as I have already mentioned concerning wounds, that every wound that is not cleansed will fester, and there is pus,

Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you should know that I will tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	There are wounds of fistula in all limbed with pain;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves.

si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you take example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There once was a young man who was about .xxx. years old, who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within his body.
