puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then bandage the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the decay is in the bone, if it is brittle and breaks easily, for as much as the corrupted bone is, it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	If you see the bone decaying, if it breaks in this place as it is before said,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then you must cure it as much as possible;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is feverish, swollen, and causes great pain, you must consider healing it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then pierce the spleen with a sharp needle through and through,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard that the wound does not go deeper than the rib which is below the spleen, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is [further] bleeding, put something above which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Two thumbs are born in the hands of some men by chance, and are always fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance they have a part where there is bone, and never a nail.</start_of_turn>
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in the bones of us two thumbs.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	they never move again.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And thus that which is born at the shoulder joint, by chance changes its position.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	its size is slight, in part only noticeable:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	its size is like that of the root of a large spindle.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the shoulder joint is grief to cure: if you keep it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	When he is born or must in the rear not, if you must copy first the round bone until the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When he is born or must at the rear not, if you must copy first the round bone until the bone, then copy the bone to a suitable breadth at this point, then cure it until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from birth, or from a wound, or from the burn of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you must copy that wound, if it must repair according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two bands or cloths soaked in rose oil, which do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two pieces of soft lead, as long as the bones are soldered, if it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When it comes to the bones of the forearm, with the palm, if they are soldered, if they are not soldered, they will break.
Des vils	Villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large blood vessels covered in greasy melancholy humours, which come with many painful swellings of the limbs.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more are found in the legs of those who walk and work and bear burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give them any purgatives of bile, and then the remainder of the nourishment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	Iron is cured in two ways: one is with vinegar and the other with soot;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And thus, if you bind up the vein and press firmly,
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	Then, if you bind up the vein and press firmly,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the limb of the patient from the buttock down to the knee joint;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then bind up the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then believe and apply force for the black blood to your hand, from the thumb to the little finger, as much as there is without causing harm to the patient who can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then hold it [the blood vessel] steady, and instruct that he grasp flesh encompassing the black vein.</start_of_turn>
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Repeat the evacuation and bleeding until the veins are full, and do no harm to the patient.</start_of_turn>
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The nourishment of this kind is as follows: renew the limb of the patient if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then he puts it in the bath, and he raises the limb of hot water until it turns red, and swells the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If there is no bath, if he throws a burn on the fire, and then puts a compress on the vein from the loin to the knee or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then he covers the skin with ointment, and tightens the vein from the armpit downwards, until it bursts when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it comes out it looks like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then stretch the limb outward, until it is free from the skin, and then close with a slight pressure,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then stretch the limb outward, until it is free from the skin, and then close with a slight pressure; then support the skin over the wound until it is closed.</start_of_turn>
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then stretch the limb outward, until it is free from the skin, and then close with a slight pressure; then support the limb at the root, as you have done before, and close with another bandage, as you did before.</start_of_turn>
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then stretch the limb outward, until it is free from the skin, and then close with a slight pressure; then support the limb at the root, and close with another bandage; then stretch the limb again, and close with a bandage at the end.</start_of_turn
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then the trace and hold until the second size; then the extraction of size by size, until it is all gone, then the closing.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not trace and lift it, if there remains an awl at every thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and hold the thread and trace, and if there are drops .i. rain, keep your hand from one side and the other, until it is gone.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and do not let it close, for if it closes, if we cannot trace or lift it, there will be damage to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have finished treating it, if you take out the limb from the wound covered with soft wool in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	When the limb is stiff and twisted and bound together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If you must bend it forcefully, but do not bind it; and treat it as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron from which the limb is bound is curved, and do not break it, only bind the vessel;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of great concern, for if it were slight, it would close the vein, but if it be great as we have said, thus is its form:
De la voinne civile	Henceforth from the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot places where there are neither herbs nor trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes from the decay that comes from the softening of the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If he comes from the belly of a serpent towards you, grasp between skin and bone.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	If there is a sign of great swelling in the limb, as when a large inflammation comes into the limb,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limb must be bound, and the swelling must be reduced like the root of a plant
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the limb is open, if it is necessary, cover with a piece of sponge about the size of three and a half fists, and the thumb,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	And let the limb hang down, and whenever it comes close to slipping out, if the covering encloses the limb and the new growth.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, if in its course a part breaks off, and covers the remainder, and do not cover it at its root, until it is entirely expelled.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, if it returns into the flesh, and causes swelling and pus or death, and makes the disease worse.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of that one must treat it promptly and promptly until it is completely gone or destroyed;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And never is this vein when treated with five palms of length, or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one hand comes out to me, from ten palms of length, and when you hold it, if there are one or two wounds or breaks, and you pierce it through to the marrow.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if it is all the same; and either empty the matter that is inside, and bring in medicines that will cause no further damage, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And never is this vein like the hands of rain, and even when it breaks in the elbow or in the wrist,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And thus comes moisture from a wound, and from a sudden leap; cure the same as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From wounds that arise between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This ailment is called in our land "buffalo disease," because it often causes swelling of the belly
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and goes up and down throughout the body,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And he feels well aware of the limb from one end to the other, as soon as it breaks the skin or moves, and jumps fiercely.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is plagued by the discharge of various humors, as blood, semen, bile, urine, or worms or pus;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and there is doubt of its malice, for when it goes through the chest and ascends to the head, and comes out at the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	it sometimes returns, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healing and treating, if it cannot be forced until it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	when you must hold the limb firmly below and above with a strong, tight tie,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	it will remain fixed without further displacement, and you will not be able to force it again.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if the fire cautery is applied, as long as it is burning;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it makes is when it breaks the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or close to the oil, immediately restrain its beard with your thumb and index finger, and grasp above and below, and pull forcefully.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and command the patient to use warm compresses of soothing herbs to eliminate bad humors from the body,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and advise the consumption of nourishing foods.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes of wind-gusts
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and because it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and found her arm swollen, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And thus afterwards, the patient will rise up like a worm on the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more stiff than anything, like living silver when it breaks from its bone to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that limb and settles in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then afterwards corrected by all the bones, so that it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted back towards the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it twisted back and forth between the limbs, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I must maintain that even though I do not wish to move the limb in pain, it still moves with great discomfort.</start_of_turn>
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not wish to do so, as I have seen her do this to many women;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought that this was the reason why the woman had dry skin and uncovered veins.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appeared that cold air was confined.</start_of_turn>
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not perceive me according to this reason those who are merry, and who have moist skin and veins that are filled again.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the cure for this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the shoulder bone above and below is affected, and then the shoulder is suddenly constrained as this wind opposes it,
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	then cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the wind that comes out of it, like foul pills and pills of serpin, and similar things.
Des saiettes	From sponges.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The bandages are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the pain or the reason for their use.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	There are various types of bandages, some with large points, small ones, feathered, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	some with angles, some with lengths, and some with pieces of cloth attached
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	or in the main joint it pricks, or in the forearm it pricks, or in the leg it pricks, or in the foot it pricks, or in the armpit it pricks, or in the groin it pricks, or in the chest it pricks, or in the belly it pricks.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	If the brain, head, liver, spleen, heart, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When they are cut, then in no limb of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must know that to extract this arrow is dangerous, for death often follows in various ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when the wound is bad, it does not tell you anything, and the arrow is not yet out of its wound, if the treatment is delayed, and the cure is made for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and jumps the scab which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when cutting and soiling and vomiting and redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes without any wound, or without ears; and sometimes loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and sometimes spurts forth white moisture resembling pus, and sometimes like burnt hair;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this sign shows you, if you persist in your cure, draw out the arrow if it is not ensnared.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	When the arrow pierces or curves, the sign is that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were fixed in something hard, do not be empty-handed;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And sometimes the arrow moves like a pulse, and causes black spots of blood, and comes with cold sweat and chills, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	There is doubt that the patient will survive.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an infected wound is that it never swells without pus leaking from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow comes out through the covering of the wound, if it is small, spit out great pain and great swelling and cries out; and moves all the limbs stiffly.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow comes out or through the stomach, by chance there is no undigested meat from the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow comes out or through the belly, and there is no sign of stool in the intestines, if there is no hope for the cure, do not attempt to extract the arrow.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the bladder stone breaks in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, the patient feels great pain: such pain as the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other members, if the face, the neck, the chest, the armpits, the groin, the thighs, the arms, and the legs are affected, and the rest of the body, they are all subject to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the bladder stone is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this I do not know what to say.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There once was a bladder stone that slipped or dripped at the root of the nerves.</start_of_turn
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and the traitor on the other side scorched the fat of the ear, and it was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And the traitor brought a sliver that fell into the fat of the ear from the marrow through the opening,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	the sliver was returned, and did not touch anything except the point towards the bottom was struck
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the sliver was as long as a Turkish arch, almost as long as an ear; the game was cured, and there was no further mishap.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And draw out a splinter from the throat to a crest, and the Arabian sponge was at the ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I saw the bristles [of the sponge], and I pulled it out as long as I could, and it was healed the crests.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew out a splinter from my cheek or belly, and I thought it was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after a few days, if it did not recover its normal state.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut across the arrow, and the bone, and the flesh, without any mishap.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if thus be the case that a wound has been caused by an arrow that has fallen out or is lodged behind, and the wound is deep;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	leave the arrow in its place, and do not alter its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor will you find any discomfort in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And thus another man, who had an arrow stuck in his face, was wounded;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and immediately suffered great pain; and there were other symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	The king’s prince had an arrow stuck in his thigh, which was causing him no small discomfort.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and there was a decline on the outer side; and the arrow was completely withdrawn
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I flee called to the care after it had been closed for two days. If I find the wound much swollen.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I would attempt to treat it with all my might, and I do not feel it myself;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was no longer any pain or tingling in her ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that this was due to the point of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place upon the limb a plaster that is both absorbent and digestive, so that the limb does not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I notice the limb is relieved of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the dressing with my hands, and closed the wound, and reassured the patient for a long time
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow was gone from his flesh; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply the corrosive medicine to the wound with my hands for as long as necessary, until it is sufficiently open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I grasp the tissue, and I feel the head of the splinter that is protruding from the wound;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I apply the medicine to the wound opening by means of that corrosive agent, until the splinter is visibly expelled from the wound;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and I will keep it covered for about three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then he widens the wound so that I can insert the nails, and I grasp it from both sides, and I cannot do otherwise.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore, I will continue to struggle and devise cunning methods like an expert, until I have secured the nails firmly in place.</start_of_turn>
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	As for what is seen at the end of this chapter, when I have finished, I will return the wound to its original state.</start_of_turn>
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or tell me what is the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you put your remedy on what I do not understand, for I cannot understand your book;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but you know your masters well enough to know about great things, and about what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Trueve neuf couver, et neuf instrument, au dessendement des choses estraanges qui arrivent en ce art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	True nine cover, and nine instruments, at the descending of strange things that happen in this art.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by loosen from the limb or they are fiched by force of other things;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps forward by itself or is forced by the flesh, is the sacket which has penetrated into the marrow, and it leaps nevermore.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	If it does not jump now, leave it until the chariot is carried around the turn, and rejoice at the issue.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	If it is firmly stuck in the bone and will not come loose, leave it be for a few days, and move it little by little each day.</start_of_turn>
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	When it finally jumps, and if it still does not jump, if you pierce around at everything around here, as long as the limb is swollen, and then withdraw it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the bone is fractured at the shoulder joint, and goes up to one of the vertebrae of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And no other accidents did I mention to the patient: if you do not treat it immediately, but leave it as it is until it becomes equal again after a few days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the scab comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	and if the scab is only fixed in the bone, and does not come up to the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains with the patient for several days without any other accident, if the swelling is treated.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is firmly stuck and will not yield, if you administer oil around the circumference, as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the scab is firmly stuck in the flesh and cannot be seen, if the pain is severe;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if the limb has no visible fracture;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you do not perceive any displacement of the wound, and for the depth of the wound,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and if there is an ear in the wound, hold it so that it does not move.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone that is stuck at the root of the limb moves when you touch it,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	break or crush the ears of the dressing, as long as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And subtilize well that you do not break the splinter, but that you carry it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it at once, if the limb remains limp at its entrance, then carry it out, for the extraction is joyful.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the evacuation of blood hinders you, do what we have said concerning the treatment in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and take care of the incision of the vein and the vein, and put something in between as you are about to pull out the splinter,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or burn, or twist, or firmly or loosely; and set the patient according to the shape he was when the arrow flew in.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you do not know how, if you do not understand what it shows you, do as it signs
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees it or feels it at once.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Take hold of it thus, until the nails can take hold, and then remove the arrow: if it now spurts out.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extruded, if you leave it hooked, and then resume the extraction until it comes out forcefully;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a splinter of bone, if you break it off, if the limb has been fractured all the way through
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if there is a chip, and you see immediately, if it has been fractured all the way through
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument; and then hold firm,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If the arrowhead gets caught in the groove of the instrument; and then hold it firmly, because if the arrow is pulled out too soon, the instrument’s point entering the flesh will ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is entangled, if you must, cover all the surrounding tissue or withdraw the poison quickly, if you must,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the splinter comes out of the eye or the cheek or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close, and you must cover over it, if you cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and cover the wound and the nerve, then take out the splinter, and then stitch the wound shut if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and keep it clean until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the nails with which we treat the saiettes is like the beak of an osprey, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many methods: great, moderate, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the end of the arm is like the quill of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push at the tip of the arrow, as is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the nails to push and to grasp if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	From veins of common cause
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins of common origin
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	namely: the jugular veins which are behind the ears, which are closed by the hair.
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two temporal arteries which are in the temples appear;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And thus veins which are in the armpits of the armpits, which are called "aspirations",
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is under the chin; and the vein that is at the base of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two cords which are under the collarbone;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the veins that are under the chin, and these are the veins that are called "augierich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And thus with veins that are soft and limp.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	And thus with veins that are soft and limp. The veins which we commonly touch are two in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The one is the cephalic, and is towards the left side of the breast, and they call it the great vein.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the other is called the “fast,” and is composed of the cephalic and axillary veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it the vein of the head; and if it is or is torn at the cost,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the vein of the head; and if it is or is torn at the cost.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one which is commonly seen to open visibly on the belly.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the savior is the vein which is between the elbow and the wrist, and if there is rain.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the limb or the heel are two veins: one if it is on the outer side of the corbicula towards the left costal cartilage.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is at the ankle towards the right costal cartilage; and the vein which is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other costal cartilage.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other limb are two veins like those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to cause old catarrh and emigration;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the quality of the patient, as I have said, is that you must rejoice in the chief of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the skin or veins are rough; then tighten the patient’s collar with a knot.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the veins open behind the ears depend from the chief:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then if you feel the pulse of your heart, if it signifies an embolism;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet and pierce the vein downwards to the bone, then hold your hand over the entire upper arm.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and hold the skin and the vein well together. It should be almost certain that the blood will spurt out, and do it until you see blood;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and the cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	is thick, sticky, and usually causes swelling, and in the midst of tears there are pus-filled boils.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the blood is like that which I have mentioned.
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient strains his neck, while the two veins open widely;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the pulse throbbing in his hand, and then he signs himself with his thumb.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then he holds his hand high above his wrist on his thumb, and he grasps the lancet in his hand.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and he seizes the vein high up, and he limps it, just as you have done with other veins, and does the evacuation of blood as needed.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then he unhooks the patient, and places his thumb on the vein, and then places a bandage;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then the thread comes out whole, and you leave it as long as it remains intact; and we have already spoken of its coming out and its extraction, or its beginning from the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that from the cephalic vein, for there are diseases of the face from ancient times, and migraine, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	When the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein bursts open.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called the “forceps,” which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point above the vein, and hold it firm with your hand, or with something else, and leave the blood flow as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient’s collar and bind the vein until it is firm and never leave the work with a wide flame.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not fitting that the flames be too great; and the same with the vessel, for the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the two veins which are about the size of almonds helps to relieve pain, swelling, tension, redness, and inflammation of the face; and has diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And if the patient pulls out his tongue by twisting from side to side, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then withdraw the tongue, and let the blood flow freely, a long distance with a broad flame, for there is no char.</start_of_turn>
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make evacuation of blood, as much as you are able, and then bind up the wound, and bind it firmly.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood of the vein does not flow if it is cold, and in fever, and in sickness of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If there is swelling and redness that comes to the face, and even if it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	if there is also bleeding of the same kind that if the patient bites his collar, then strain his jaw to your left hand.</start_of_turn>
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the burning flame long, and hold it in the space between the nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the blood vessel must not be burnt more than two palm-widths; and when it is on the fire, it must not move at all.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not delay too long in making the incision, and do it as much as necessary; then bind it for one night, for it is often restored by morning.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	For the fire cautery:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The fire cautery is useful for the treatment of swelling, bruising, infection, inflammation, and various diseases, such as herpes and stomach ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	If the patient pulls out his hair at the root, as we have mentioned before.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master be above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on his seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then hold the vein long and widely open, and prick the blood gently, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same in the other vein, and loosen the thread, and hold the blood vessels moderately tight,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins from the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and swelling and pain.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then open the vein, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the limb and the other on the left side,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And one knows them by this, that they are black, and by this, that they have small veins running black inside them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So do the one with the other, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if the greatest part of the armpit is black, and also do the veins beneath and above, because this is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the veins of the armpit the tongue is black.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins that are beside the tongue is of aid after the blood of the cephalic; and this is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth.

saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood therefore goes up and down, and do not go too far apart, for these are the arteries.

Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone is seen by the physician, in whatever way, if it is commanded that he be bled to relieve a fever,
