Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And if the patient is suffering from acute pain in the belly, and is vomiting profusely,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	Then the belly becomes swollen like a barleycorn, and from under the joint pain shoots out like rain
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Then the belly becomes swollen like a barleycorn, and from under the joint pain shoots out like rain, either blood or something like blood, at the ankle or further down, causing great pain.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you see blood on the hand, if you are wary of the nerves that are sore, and if the limb has been cut as if by a sword; or the flame is near.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be cured, if you reset the bone in water, and leave the vein wide open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If it must be done again, do it for the first time, and if you do it again later, because the limb is stiff;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt, as we have said, and take an equal amount of soothing from the other limb.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the buttock, and its blood is worth as much as the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that comes out.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And if the patient is between the urine and the bowels, and is straining below the ankle for three times in bending,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	otherwise it does not open the belly; and if it does open, if the patient is in any way unable, or if he travels.</start_of_turn>
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is better to keep it closed, because the belly is soft and easily restored by hand.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	and if you do not find it, if some other wound opens or does burst, and towards the little toe, and take care of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And do so diligently with blood that you see, and then loosen the tie, put on a bandage and hold it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	And do so diligently with blood that you see, and then loosen the tie, put on a bandage and hold it; it is now healed.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	And do so diligently with blood that you see, and then loosen the tie, put on a bandage and hold it; it is now healed
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And do so diligently with blood that you see, and then loosen the tie, put on a bandage and hold it; it is now healed.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And ventilation which is made by cutting and by extracting blood if it is done in twelve days with care,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	And ventilation which is made by cutting and by extracting blood if it is done in twelve days with care, for in that time one is all over the head and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And twelve other in twelve costs of the neck; and the head is filled with wind;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the chest is filled with wind; and the chest above the ribs;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the bumps swell up both arms; and the bumps swell up both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the bumps swell up both wrists; and the swelling does not affect blood, except for the great veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	because of this it does not make a man bleed, as when we make a vein bleed
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it does not cause him to bleed, neither with great heat nor without, in any disease that comes from congestion, as long as all the swellings are drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity or custom dictates, if the attendants must stay awake for some hours at the beginning or at the end, and during every tension;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they must stay awake, suffer from a heavy head.</start_of_turn>
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if at such times they find swelling and redness in their face, and in their head and neck, and darkness in their eyes.</start_of_turn>
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find blood dripping from their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and vomit blood.</start_of_turn
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if he has such ones who think, and sees by nut blood and navrates and blood and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and the patient is in a state of great fear and distress, we command him to fast for two hours.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The patient’s blood if it helps with the chief … that comes from the eruptions of the eyes, and we must not do anything until after the evacuation of all the humors.</start_of_turn
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	if it is in place of the cephalic blood,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not suitable for me to perform this treatment on someone who has a cold complexion or who has a rash, because this causes them great discomfort.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason I am not suitable for this treatment except for the old who have or suffer from cold diseases.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if those who are well-versed in the matter disagree, and for this reason it is necessary to place the ventouse somewhat lower due to the doubt of compliance.</start_of_turn
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suctions on the collar are in lieu of blood and bile, and for this reason they are worth more than gold.</start_of_turn>
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And at a fissure of the channel below the ear, and at all points, and at repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is certain to press there, for if it holds too tightly, if in vain it resists or causes swelling or pain.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The winds blow cold as cold as the collar of a coat if worth the pain of the head, and pain in the temples, and swelling, and strangulation, and toothache.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in lieu of the blood of the basilisk; and command the patient to express his hand to put it in, that he does not cut the artery, and does not withdraw blood unnecessarily.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow over the mouth if it is sick with mouth disease, and with corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the cause of the health of the teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the south blow over the teeth if it is sick from heat and swelling
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the south blow over the tongue if it is sick as much as two veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to fear too much pain, for his blood is of charcoal, and he knows bones and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the buttocks is worth having haemorrhoids from the foundation, and has diseases of bones and arteries; and it is recommended that the swelling be large and of hair, that it has much to do with well-treating; and by chance, if it should be ruptured, there will be great wounds
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs are apt to open widely, because they attract blood from all over the body, and cause old pains of the veins, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and reinforce the flowers; and are in place of the spleen, and the kidneys, and all of them cause the body to swell up later on, and cause vomiting of blood in various situations.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is as follows: if you apply it at first glance, and do so promptly, and put it on firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing so until you see the blood flow red and swelling, and open the wound; then withdraw, and take care of the patient’s condition, for there are some who have a tender scar, and clear pores: if you must cut once alone, and you must make large wounds, and a deep wound; and do so cautiously.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not large, if you must cut once: the first time to staunch the flow of blood from the large vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is very thick, if you must cut three times; and when our wings grow weary of blood, if we only suffer once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if our veins burst with blood, if we recommence too often; and if without hope we are pierced in the heart, if we finish when the pain is perceived without delay.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it befits the one who has thick skin and tough hair, and who has numerous boils, that you order the loosening of the veins with an aperitif and dissolving oil
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if that is in this state, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	or if it is in ivy, with horseradish oil, or lavender, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluous moisture is great and cold, take olive oil of marigold, or balsamite, or olive oil of anet, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the skin is tightly stretched and has large pores, do not put oil on it,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but you must wash it afterwards with rosewater, or cold water, or elderberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or something similar.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it easily rises, or of mistletoe, and sumac, and the like.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive superficial sweating rise from wine strong, or from seawater, or from decoction of elderflower or chamomile, or from other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and do not feel safe with the suction cup before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the suctioning.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and must be warned when it is necessary to suction and when it is suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take care that those who are being suctioned are not too cold or too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is suspected that he has taken cold things, like pomegranates, grapes, turnips and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and meat juices, fat and moist meats.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, if he takes honey syrup, and fragrant wine medium, which is between summer and autumn, and broth, and meat juices and small oils and herbs.</start_of_turn>
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when the air is cold, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is fitting to give some comfort to the principal members once the wound has been dressed, neither before nor afterwards, by the blowing air; for this will soothe the limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Or let it be simply taken away, but it is not fitting for me to do anything except for those who are in charge of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The patches that are applied to the wound are those that are put on the liver, and on the mouse, and under the heel, and on the belly and the butt and the groin and the hip, for these members do not suffer from wounds elsewhere.</start_of_turn
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one should not do it except to draw blood from limb to limb,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	If we place our thumbs on the limb when it does not bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, if we place compresses on the belly and the buttocks to calm the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and soothe the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, if it comes by its natural attraction by an adventure of the swelling, or discharge the stone from its place
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and make it swell when we place it on the liver and the spleen when there is retained moisture.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these compresses are administered empty in order to soak as little as possible; and never are they administered together with fire, and never completely filled with liquid.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	If there are diseases of the chest or the belly, and in such a way that the wounder fills the ventouse with hot water or with water itself, or where there are herbs covering that.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the ventouse administered to fire is like this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And has two large and half palms of diameter, and has or costs almost half an inch in the middle, as to push out an arrow,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	or be of linen, soft before so that it does not hurt the patient when putting it on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there was in the middle a stick of iron or thorn, to hold a bandage firmly in place.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there were great and small ones according to the ailments and the severity of those who took them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the wounds of the sick are different from those of the healthy, and the leanings are different from the fats.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	and must one place this bandage upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Grasp the handle of the circular saw or line it, and put it into the ventouse through the hole which is in the ventouse.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If it sticks at the bottom of the ventouse, it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	then put it on the limb, and two must be on the hole we mentioned above, if when you look, if it goes up, take away the ventouse.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and grasp the lining like before, and start again, if you are able.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse where it is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all sharpness, there is no bulge or perforation, and is administered only when it is plain of sharpness, and is placed on the limb only slightly.
et c’est li forme:	and thus is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	They are not administered for other members or where we cannot place ventouses because of their small size, as with livers and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the like of them stripped of hair, as with dogs or nails, and others like these;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and the quality of the patient is such that when you find hairs that are in soft, smooth waves without any curvature, if you pluck them out;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then immediately take hold of the limb and make it pale, and rub the limb until it is red, and put on the hairs;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are smooth and gentle, and chirpy, if it is possible to put on a suction cup, put it on, for this is worth more later.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, if you lift the limb easily, and then with some force, moisten well, and then expel it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb remains too long after the evacuation of the foreign body, moisten it with cold water, and put on, until the swelling is reduced;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swelling persists, put on broken glass or pieces of crucible, and similar things, until the swelling is reduced.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you take out half of the black beans and leave them until they are burned on the limb, if you stop it now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you are in doubt, take other signs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	Or if the signs do not suffice, rub the limb with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle until the sign is seen.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them back, and as soon as they feel blood returning;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are healed, if you powder over a wound of aloe and sow, or charcoal, if they will now be cured.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Ci comence li livre des brisures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.</start_of_turn>
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen well, dear son, for this chapter deals with a matter that is not mentioned in any of the former books, and is not found in any letter.</start_of_turn
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	Therefore, in our land, this science is strange, for I have never found anything like it.</start_of_turn
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except by the wisdom of the ancient books, or because I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	I have described it in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the previous chapters
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters or the knowledge that it contains, and that we remain true, so that those who are learned and who learn this noble art may learn from it and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain occurs, if you must hasten the patient's recovery, do not neglect anything that does not harm him, even if he is weak of body, a child, or an old man.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if he is too tense or too cold; and eat cold broth, that is to say cold juices, broth of barley and eggs, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have certainty that the patient will recover.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, if you must nourish the patient with foods that cause great nourishment, or if he has viscosity, as with wheat flour in water, rye, peas, almonds, cheese, fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at a part nourishment returns muscle and more tension the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken from marrow and decrepit do not mend well together according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too brittle, like bones of small intestines;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no remedy, remain upon the broken bone, that is, great tensions that hold and unite the limb together, as much as it forces it if it had been before; and do not remove any part of it, for by this means it is expedient to nourish large amounts of flesh, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the limb, or of the foot, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.</start_of_turn>
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.</start_of_turn
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And there is a certain cunning that has its own instrument and restoration, as he remembers when he comes to it.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that a break of a bone is when its limb is twisted, and it opens well by pushing, and sometimes by the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know whether it is moving or not, but put on medicines that come later, and then strain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And so it is said that when the bladder bursts and goes down into the bowels, and is made up of these two parts of the joint, it is necessary to put them together evenly, even as if it were a postumous bruise.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the bruise comes again, if you leave it alone, until the bruise is appeased;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it into its place as gently and steadily as you can, and so that the bladder is restored more easily than by restoring the limb or parts of it; and then tighten it, as you would afterward
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	and if there are broken pieces of bone, if they are two parts of the hand or foot, or at the wrist or two fingers, or an artery, or a vein and the hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb break, remember by all means the adjuncts in their place at the muscle as you wish, and keep that by your work no damage comes to the patient from lesion or pain.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the joints of the bones according to the best forms
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if you think it is not well: if it is swelling well, and it is not straining too much, do not press as those who do who make it come by their work excessive heat and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is fixed in place, if the patient is very sick and does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, neither turning nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and keep it firmly secured that he feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at the point [of dislocation], and you must put it in partial control that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it correctly positioned, that there be no displacement when you restore it;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of a broken limb is as I have said.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The quality of a broken limb is diverse in small, medium, and large sizes and shapes
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as bones of the arm and forearm and similar: if you can cover them with soft cloths and blankets;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and for those that are large, such as thighs and legs: if you can cover them with a broad and hard cloth, because the large cloths embrace the whole great limb, and constrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lie down comfortably, with legs slightly flexed, two or three according to the limb, and hold your hand one inch from the tip, then go under the break and strain less, than the break, then remove one inch of the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb somewhat, so that you can grasp a great part of the limb, then retake one inch of the limb, and turn back slightly from the break;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go under the break at the lower part, and strain moderately, not too strong or too weak, as we said before;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the layers of cloth or bandages, as many as are even, and bind them securely with thread; and put your stakes well made above, if there is no puncture or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or puncture, put above something soothing the puncture, and which breaks the swelling, and leave it for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your stakes, and let them be half of a broad sickle in length, or of staff from which you make nails, or of barley straws, and let them be as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the one who sets the fracture put something on the break that is greater and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and is also as long as it is necessary for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then it is strained upon the bones just as you did at first, and then you tie under a thread immediately, as you did on the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is tight under the thread, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and be of linen cloth.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their braids from twisted linen thread, this is a great error, for the braid cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it will not hold together unless there is at least a cubit of space between the knots.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is numbed by the blows of the needles after the stretching, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, they will not bleed
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a bruise, and the nerve is severed, I will tell the cure of that later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And as regards those who do not wish to endure this discomfort, they must immediately break the limbs the first moment.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not permissible for me to apply the stars except after five or seven days, or more as seems suitable; otherwise, the wound will burst forth.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And concerning the management of ancient compresses to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take flour that is held in the mill’s walls, and mix it with abundant eggs, and make this confection, neither too fine nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of restoring fracture at various stages, and even among women and young children, for there is neither too much pressure nor too much cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed and alum and saffron and Arabic gum and mugwort, all in the amount of eight; mirrace and aloes, in the amount of five; chamomile, in the amount of seven; and grind them together, and mix them with abundant eggs; for if the complexion of the patient is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other means of support that are worth considering are: mugat and vismalve, with .x. grains; mirre and aloes, with .viiij. grains; acaice vi. grains; and arnica root powder .x. grains, and grind thoroughly, and mix with water or a great deal of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other means of support that are worth considering are: mugat and vismalve, with x grains; mirre and aloes, with viiij grains; acaice vi grains; and arnica root powder x grains, and grind thoroughly, and mix with water or a great deal of egg, and administer. Such plasters do not restore health, but they are good for soothing post-burn pain, and for strengthening bones that are out of place.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other means of support that are worth considering are: dried fig tree leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, ground together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Autre méthode d’emplaustre à la restauration de la brisure de l’os et pour amenuisier le reste de l’apostème. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, fleurs de violettes, farine de fois, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se le membre est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of support for the restoration of a broken bone and to diminish the rest of the abscess. Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violets, wheat flour, and from chescune one part; grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with moist coriander water or with water alone, and use.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras writes in his book that there is no need to put anything on the broken limb to restore its force except for a little wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and firm.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen would have us put on the warm parts of the member broken, to restore things dry a little warm, as for example, myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped almonds, or pine needles, and gum, and mix them evenly, and crush them, and make a dressing of them and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then loosen a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, that the bone is not fractured; if not, loosen by hand at first.</start_of_turn>
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain comes to the limb, or if it swells, sense repose or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen it and place the limb in its proper position now; take a light bandage, a sponge soaked in salt, and immerse in water, and raise the limb until the swelling ceases and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry lint, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind up with a nut, until you are certain that the swelling has gone down
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then rest the inflamed limb, and if there is pain, then rejoin the bandage, and a little displacement, do not bind too tightly; and be careful until you are healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see swelling, redness, pain, and swelling about the bone, it is necessary to support and bind, if it recurs, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing happens to the limb after what we have said, if it does not swell within two, three, five, or seven days; do not leave it for twenty days, as we have seen, until the swelling subsides, and approach the closing of the wound cautiously.</start_of_turn>
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore the more restraint you put on it than before, and the more you grease the flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the limb is drying out more than usual, do not expect that the wounds will heal.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Arise, then, with hot water steaming, whenever you loosen it, and every time that you touch it, and cut a little bit of the cord;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Rise then, with hot water steaming, every time you loosen it, and every time you touch it, and cut a little bit of the cord; for in this work, the limb is often loosened from the bone, and the patient must immediately mend what the fools make, lest it remain twisted: that is wrong, and if there is great fear, I see no other thing but to leave it alone and cut directly.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	various ways of breaking.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many are the ways of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone throughout the bone until the cartilage which is between the bones, as if made by a chisel or a fist; and for this reason it is called this kind of fracture "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone in a transverse direction, and is called this kind of fracture "absolue"; and is the wound of these large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the bone, or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the socket which is below the bone, or it is on the bone, then this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is embedded in the bone just under the skin, and the break is small, it is called a “capillary” fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is made or pierced by a stone, or by a thorn, or by something similar, and it causes a fragment of the bone to protrude, and if the limb is bent as when people make a stew over a cauldron; if between the bone fragments.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this often happens to people who have or suffer from moist bones, like children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are many other ways of fracture when small pieces are detached from them as in these; and I will speak of them later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And there are many other ways of fracture when small pieces are detached from them as in these; and I will speak of them later.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary resemblance is known by this that when one has discovered the bone, and has wiped around it, if one finds a black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s accidents and if you see no other bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, paleness, fever, and swelling, and other similar things, if it does not recover sense immediately.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you suspect no imminent danger, and hope for recovery, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes forward first, and it is in swelling, if you can remove the bone before the fourth part of the muscle that you must do so.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you hurry to remove the bone before the seventh part of the muscle, so that the tissue of the bone is corrupted, there will come the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	If the bone breaks through to the tissue that covers the brain, if you can manage to split the fractured part, and take hold of the limb of the patient, and uncover the bone in every way that you can, and on the figure of the wound more strongly than you can.</start_of_turn
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flows from a vein when uncovering the bone, or from an abscess, let him hold fast what he can; and fill the wound with soft cloths moistened with oil of roses.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And keep the abscess quiet until the swelling subsides; then, when the bone is well supported, do the work in two ways: the one way is if you grasp the narrow end of the wound in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then do another incision more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have various sizes of testicles, some large and others small, and they are pointed and made of iron, and in their lighter work, do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through it, even though you administer testicles with tarres, do not pierce beyond the test bone. And you must leave above the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that if the testicles come out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have several tarres on the test; and this is the form of the two methods of tarring.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put one tarret on the bone, and turn your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the tarret back in another place a little later, and do the same thing to the surrounding area, and cut between the perforations, and do it more skillfully than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have if you have them, pincers; and keep your hands away from the brain and the jawbone.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have grasped the bone firmly, and treated, if it is possible, restore the fragment that has separated from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more rigid and flexible than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if nothing of the small bones remains, no teeth, if the bones are slightly loose with instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of working is like the Galenicians say, which is more certain; and the lord is very strong, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either by fracture or by opening the muscle, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put back the head of this lenticular incisor, for this is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Do not split into two parts, and is the part that is tough in the marrow, if the cutting is towards the bone; then hold with a small mallet above, so that you press lightly the bone all around, and take care of the membrane that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is torn from the bone, if the bone is lightly fractured, for we must fracture it well steadily, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks through the skin, do not pierce it further with a needle; cut it off just below the fracture, and there will be small pieces left. If you suspect infection, remove the surrounding tissue with a scraper or file of various sizes, in order to prevent infection in each place, according to the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the fracture is great and after more scraping, and does not cease, do it until it is well healed.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and fracture of a subtle kind, it is necessary to bring about the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not put his study into this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the swelling is discovered, it is best that you take one and a half draping of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in oil rose, and put it upon the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another drape of doubled linen, or two, and moisten it in wine and oil rose, and put it on the first drape; and do this more gently than you think, that you do not aggravate the swelling, then administer further linen, and do not keep it bound more tightly than is necessary to hold the wound in place only.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for one or two hours, until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines such as root of licorice, flour of sometimes, and incense dust, and an astringent; mix these things together, and put them on the wound, and administer adequate medicines all around the wound area.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And beware that the wound is properly closed, that you do not leave it open, neither do you leave it partially assembled, for when it is assembled over the brain, if it is crooked or taut, it causes great harm to the patient; for when one puts on the teeth of biting things, if they do not desist from below.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if any evil event comes to the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt, it is doubtful sense.</start_of_turn>
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the evil does not come forth only by the medicine that we have put on, that some virtue has, if you can take a part of honey, and two parts of rose oil and glue one with the other, and put it on the wound;

Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say no restorer must soak the tents in water, and leave each one to itself. And never do they put goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is sulfur powder draped around, and it is held in place, and blows the patient among them; or do as you see fit.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if they come to rest while you are working, if you put some butter or cotton soaked in rose oil or some such salve on it.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if after that the swelling does not subside, if you put on a compress of hempseed meal, fine flour, and incense powder, confirmed with a raw egg yolk, then put on soft bandages, and do not bind too tightly;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the swelling does not go down after that, if you put on a compress of hempseed meal, fine flour, and incense powder, confirmed with a raw egg yolk, then put on soft bandages, and do not bind too tightly;
