de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and the break is only slight, and is not broken through, except for the teeth inside, if one knows it slightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is advisable, if the break is on the outer part, to bite down on the thumb of the affected hand towards the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left mandible, if you hold the thumb of the right hand, and gently hold the break inwards, and hold the other hand outwards, and make them even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the mandible is displaced, that is to say, if it is displaced by .ij., it is advisable that you administer an extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth causes pain, or a dislocation, if strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a broken mandible cerote on and put on an i. two-fold drape; and on the drape put a large sponge well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie on the suture that you put in place, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure is changing, if the bone comes loose at the third joint, and then reset it to its place; and put on a dressing of powdered alum with abundant egg or oatmeal, after you have oiled the cerote; and put on a dressing of linen. If the dressing becomes loose, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it as it is until it is healed; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if after suppuration the limb remains swollen, as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, repair so that neither part of the bone is left unboned; if delicate of the bone has instruments that cover this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if the swelling has flared up as you need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have boned all these parts, and there is no longer any displacement, if the wound is wide, put on some dressings that cover this, to absorb blood, until it is healed
de la forcele	so strong.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and the fracture is deemed to be in two ways: either it is broken and split into three pieces, and is the most light to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is with a wound, if you have two assistants, let one hold the limb that feels the strong force; and the other extend the shoulder towards the part; then set the fracture even, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no bulge or protrusion.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of wax, or linen, of the size you need; and stretch and hold the forcele, and strain the ball in your hand, so that you can put the fracture even, as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to push the head of the shoulder back in its place, because it comes out of its socket, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his side, and put a cushion under the shoulder blade, namely the middle rib, and hold the shoulder blade down until the head of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris, if you must, make an incision; and force the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot join together by any means, if there is a fracture at one of the incisors that you have made; but that you put a cushion under the shoulder to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and seems like a scoop, and is neither thin nor thick, and be as wide as it seems necessary, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured that the incision is deep enough, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the depth of the incision, if necessary employ a dressing and bandage, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the wound comes open again, if there is much blood, apply oil of rose, alum, and wine, and place above.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stiffness of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of wheat and egg-shell, and put on supports loosely above, and put a sponge below if you need it.</start_of_turn
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great bend of a palm of large size, and put two layers of cloth over the wound, and press it down firmly; then take a needle about two fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage remains in place.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Put the needle on the bone, and twist the bandage over the collar, and grasp the inner ankle, and grasp the outer ankle; and keep the part above steady, and when you see that the bandage holds the bone in place, and you see clearly that the needle does not move from the broken bone, if you praise each joint, and when you tighten the bandage.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And make the patient lie on his back, and put under his buttock one small pillow, to lift up the limb; if you align the break of the bone with the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it until it is well healed, for about twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it has to be done, and hold it and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it has to be done, and hold it and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is dislocated or hangs loose in the socket, and it cannot be forced out except by touching it; if the limb appears according to the shape of the dislocation, and is reduced according to its natural form, in all ways as you wish; then put on the limb a coarse powder of mill-flour with abundant egg white, and bandage loosely, and put on a large and firm bandage, a little wider than the shoulder, and when the bandage is set, do not move the limb, and look at the limb every hour; and every time it swells, if you tighten the bandage, and equal the bandage if it has moved from its place, and leave the patient lying on their side; and the shoulder is restored in about twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if the limb is flexible, and the patient is able to move, because it is not a bone that is easily loosened.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone hangs forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone itself, do as we have said in the bursting of the forcele to appease the pain of incision.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone hangs forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone itself, do as we have said in the bursting of the forcele to appease the pain of incision.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is never broken in the middle, but this happens often; but it often breaks with violent movement. And when it is broken in the middle, if it declines at the root, and causes the patient great pain, and swelling, and vomiting, and sometimes blood, and opens the wound in the broken bone, and they feel well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae together, and reassemble the ribs at your hands, and subtly bring into equal all the ways you can, until the bone is set as it should; then put on bandages and stamp under the staple of salt, or other soft substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind on the bone break, if it does not move; and turn the limb round about the back, and strain gently, and reward chest pain an hour later, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if it will not come loose, by corrosion or by purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, if you are in a hurry, and it comes loose, loosen the bandage, and rasp off the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then rest the dressing, and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	And the restoration is this: if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades together, and reassemble the ribs at your hands, and subtly bring into equal all the ways you can, until the bone is set as it should; then put on bandages and stamp under the staple of salt, or other soft substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind on the bone break, if it does not move; and turn the limb round about the back, and strain gently, and reward chest pain an hour later, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if it will not come loose, by corrosion or by purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, if you are in a hurry, and it comes loose, loosen the bandage, and rasp off the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then rest the dressing, and strain until it is healed.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The breaks of the ribs only come from the great joints below the back, and at the shoulder, and do not happen for anything other than because they are slimy; and the patient feels well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And if the restoration is that you put equal pressure, as it should be. Then put the support, and bind with an elastic, if you have need of it.

And if the fracture of the ribs is downward, if the patient feels great pain, and swelling, as with pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; and there is swelling, and vomiting, and a great discharge of blood, which is a great grief, and they have put much pain on it.</start_of_turn>
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said of these things that it is necessary to administer food that inflates the belly, to push out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after the catarrh has passed, life does not come back by itself.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, let it be well.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one puts on a bandage on the limb to soak up moisture, for it is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not retain the excess moisture on the limb due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse linen soaked in oil, and put on tents between the ribs to make the layer even, then either cure the pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the navel, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is commanded to cut above the broken rib, and to put in [a] sponge; then one must cut the bone lightly, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges, as long as it is healthy. And if there is pus coming from the abscess, if one puts on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and puts on the limb; and cure while the limb is held in place, as long as the rib is not displaced or it must.
de la brisure dou col	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the navel, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is commanded to cut above the broken rib, and to put in a sponge; then one must cut the bone lightly, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges, as long as it is healthy. And if there is pus coming from the abscess, if one puts on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and puts on the limb; and cure while the limb is held in place, as long as the rib is not displaced or it must be displaced from its fracture.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a fracture of the bone of the collar, and often it rains; and also at the thorn of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to no avail, and you see that he will be well or not, if you take heed if you see his hands limp, fleeing and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if he does not feel it. Such are the signs that he is in a mortal condition in many positions, and if you move him and he feels well when you strain and point, such are the signs that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if we put him to the cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when such things happen on the spine, and you see that he will be well or not, if you take heed if his fingers are soft and his hands are swollen, and if there is a wound on his back that is vomiting violently and involuntarily; and when we have bound him on his belly, if he is vomiting involuntarily. And when he is bound on his back and he sees his wound selling, if he cannot move. Such are the signs that he is in a mortal condition: if he does not work in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this does not happen, if the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that if there is a wound at the edge of the bone, put upon the spine oil of rose or oil of nutmeg of an egg, until it is calmed; then put upon one of the comfortable and absorbent plasters, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if a bone breaks, if you cover on the limb; and stretch the bone, then assemble the two ends of the wound, if it is great, with a splint, and bind it up securely; and if the fragment of the bone is broken, which is called the "break of the marrow", if it is in your left hand pouch, and put it equal to the right hand at your side, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you have need of it; then strain it, and if there are broken bones underneath, if you leave it there, and stretch the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	...and if the thigh bone is fractured...
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, if there is no other wound at the head; and if it persists, and declines downward, and comes to the patient great pain, swelling, and inflammation of that which is fractured.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over the fracture, until you reach the break; and take hold of the broken fragments and their position; and if the break is only at the head, if you make the break even, until it is in its natural position.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is on the side or it declines downwards, if you make the patient sit on his belly, until the restoration of this break is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have placed the limb even, if you place on the support, then place on a staple of lead or copper, and strain the bandage, so that it does not move; and use the thumb and index finger to hold the limb steady, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swelling comes, do not touch it, until the swelling subsides; then put on what we have said before; and then return to rest, and strain it as it should be strained, if there is no other mishap; and this is the method.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And so there are two methods for restoring it: one is to take one fist full of moistor and hold the patient’s arm above their seat; then bend the patient’s arm towards the shoulder, and put a curve in the fist, and then put the fist on no weight or have the assistant hold it down; and put the eyes level with the hands clasped together, until the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to support the patient’s shoulder and tie the arm to their collarbone, and command the assistants to hold what is on the dislocation at their hands, and to hold down the scapulae at their sides.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is too violent, strain [the limb] so that the bristle [bone spicule] is grasped by the bone on both sides. And if the bristle is close to the head of the shoulder, grasp that the middle bristle of the shoulder and another towards the elbow, grasp the bristle; and if the bristle is towards the elbow, grasp that the lightest, with effort, as long as the bristle is even on both the shoulder and the elbow; then set the bristle even, if possible, and strain, since the aftershocks do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if after-shocks come, do not strain for more than thirteen days; put on a thick dressing of lint and rose oil until the after-shocks are calmed; then strain, and the way to strain is that you place the bandage over the bristle, then assemble the limb on the shoulder and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; put on the bandage and strain the limb, and the arm will be in its place, without anything hindering it, or without the bone being fractured.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and place on the bristle a splint that is wider and stronger than the others, and put between the splints two pieces of wood that are equal in size to the thickness of the bristle; then strain on the splints, as I have said above in the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the swelling of the shoulder blade and the tightening of the muscles, as we have said, when restoring the limb, if you doubt the completeness of the cautery, leave it bound for seven days as we have said; then watch for two days whether the swelling subsides and the pain disappears from the limb, or whether the swelling returns to the limb because it is too tight.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such thing happens, if more than two days have passed, and the patient sleeps on his back with his hands on his stomach; put a cushion made of equal wool under the limb, and watch for an hour or two to see if the limb remains rigid or if the ligaments are softened; if the latter, treat it by medical means and do as we have suggested, in part by giving the limb its natural mobility. And when it begins to recover, if it is considerable. It is customary that the assistant and the limb must be kept bound for forty days in total; and then it must be loosened and a bath and medicinal poultices must be given to the limb to restore it to its proper condition. And if the fracture is difficult and embedded, it must be left to loosen for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	In the event that the arm is fractured,
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". One is small and the other is large. The small one is inside and the large one is outside; sometimes the large bone breaks alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is fractured, the restoration is easy and the healing; but when the large bone is fractured, the healing is poor and more painful than when they are fractured together. If only the small bone is fractured, if necessary extend it slightly and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is fractured, if the grip is increased; and extend over one cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the other, and the small one must be lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arms over himself, with one cushion in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the forearm to the outside of the hand, or at the elbow, and another assistant at the other side. And then set the bones even, as best you can
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture the limb is split into pieces, if one puts in a pin without removing any splinter that may be left in, and you cannot remove it, you must leave it and let it heal naturally as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, as I have mentioned in the singular chapter; take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if at the beginning of the restoration comes after the dressing, glue together with oil rose and white wax; and bind tightly but not too tightly or too loosely; and keep bound tightly by hand until the dressing has settled.  Then oil the bone and wax, and put in the dressing of meal with much egg white, for put in the nails, and let the nail of the fracture be more firm, and a hole wider than the others; and soak that it must have between the nails or arms multiple arrangements: either that the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and is more strained above the fracture than elsewhere, and all the days less in aligning, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, which is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If other evils follow the limb, as when there is itching, if you must raise the limb with warm water, until the itching ceases; and leave the limb still. Then repeat the stretching, and when the ligament is softened and the bone is loosened, and similar things, if necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the swelling does not come back to the limb, because it is too tight, if you must soften it somewhat, and leave it for some days, until the swelling goes down, and then strain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of these things that we have said help the patient, if not until after .xx days, or more, then he should rest his hands on his collar, and keep his collar even; and take care of movement and discomfort, and sleep on his back; and give him nourishment when the swelling has gone down, in .xxx days or .xxxv., or even in .xx days, according to the compositions and constitutions of the virtues.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de la main	From the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the fracture of the hand: At the back of the hand there are two bones that often break; and it does not come out but pours out many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or split, if it is known that the patient is limping, if he is sitting straight before him equally; then put his hand on the extended cloth and stretch out the broken bones, and put them even with the thumbs, until they are well joined; and put on the plaster and the bandage, if the abscess does not come out, then put on a splint as much as is necessary; and be wrapped in one cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the edge of the limb towards the belly of the hand, if you make a loop of bandage, and command the patient to hold his broken limb firmly; and then stretch from a long cloth, and be the splint as great as the bone of the hand, and strain it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is on the side, then command that you place a splint above and below at the root, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and seal the gap between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture does not come from either side, if it is the pouch, if it is equal, as it should be; and strain with the root, and if you see that it does not move, put a right splint small enough to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is elsewhere, as in the index or one of the others, if it is equal, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or bind them all together, holding the wrist tightly, or put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in restoring and disposing of the wound, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken limb
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and it is well seen when they twist before and behind; and the restoration is when it is bound with a thread above the fracture and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is within the bone itself
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the thigh, if either the upper or lower ligament of the fracture is grasped, and the other is below the fracture. And in the same way if it is close to the knee, and in this case either the upper or lower ligament of the limb is grasped, and the other is below; then put the thumbs of both hands at the same level as the natural position of the limb, and then put on the dressing and bind it, without causing any displacement.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess that has burst, let it rest peacefully and then return to your work and your treatment; the bandage is made in a timely manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	If there is an abscess that has burst, let it rest peacefully and then return to your work and your treatment; the bandage is made in a timely manner.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is an abscess that has burst, if it comes loose, address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to extract them; and if this cannot be done, it is necessary to cut the limb open and drain the pus.  The treatment is as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this place where I put the needles, as in the arm or the shoulder; nevertheless, in the restoration made in this place, I do not cause any pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the swelling that remains in the bone is restored in one or two days, or less or more, according to the variations of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the rue du genouil</start_of_turn
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	The swelling in the rue du genouil often breaks, but it rains many times. And if it breaks, it is not but a tear, or a break, and there is pain, and this is well known.</start_of_turn>
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is set right, do this: put everything that is round back to its place until it is firmly assembled again; then put on the dressing, and put on a round cushion, if you need it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the orders that we have said before, as for example incision and other like that; if you put into practice each of these things that it should be done, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if it is set right, do this: put everything that is round back to its place until it is firmly assembled again; then put on the dressing, and put on a round cushion, if you need it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the orders that we have said before, as for example incision and other like that; if you put into practice each of these things that it should be done, until it is healed.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And if it is set right, do this: put everything that is round back to its place until it is firmly assembled again; then put on the dressing, and put on a round cushion, if you need it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the orders that we have said before, as for example incision and other like that; if you put into practice each of these things that it should be done, until it is healed. As for the fracture of the limb that has three bones, one is called the "muscle" and the other is called the "fossa"; and there is all together a breaking as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is the same as that of the arm.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are fractured together, twist the limb from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured near the surface, twist the limb forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if a large bone is fractured, if one sees great pain and it is visible; and twist downwards. Then bring extension, and make it even, and tie the bones even; however, if the fracture is severe, and there are more pieces, even if extension is less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take .ij. strips of coarse cloth that cover the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the knee to the toes; then wrap in .ij. layer of lint from under and from over, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not bend either to the right or to the left, and that is good; and no one will administer any more than .ij. dose of pain that is long as the limb, and if there is a wound, and put on the limb to prevent movement, and do it properly in the fracture or there is an injury; and move each joint of the limb, to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones at their root.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but in the bones of the root of the limb there is no fracture at all, and two must suffice; there is no other means than to wait until healing is complete.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the root of the limb, and you see these bones pressing against each other, if you put the limb so that it hangs down to the earth like a bird in flight, and then put the limb back in its place, as soon as the bones are raised, then put on the dressing and bandage, and put a little bandage under the limb at the joint, then restrain the limb from moving, and cover it with a cloth bandage.</start_of_turn
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is healed, because you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are two fractures, if you restore them as we have said, then hold the hand still; then place under the fracture a splint according to the length of the fracture, and make it wider than the width of the fracture, and put on the dressing that I have said; and if there are three or more, fracture them and place under each fracture a splint according to its quantity, covered with a bandage of linen, and strain the dressing from the bone.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember that you must not neglect the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	from the fracture of the clavicle bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman are fractured, if she sits enlarged, then lean her forward; and support her behind; then fill the belly of the wound with wool, and put as much in as a sto; then draw out the woman, and keep her back and front; and then jump up the wool, until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and return the bone with the sto; and when she sees her piss, if she has pulled out the wool, and when she has pissed, she will recover; for she will make thirty-nine days or more. If the fracture is restored, and you see it, take a bladder of birch, and tie a cord to her belly, and pour all the bladder into the wound; then blow in the cord until the bladder is expelled: the wound will then return to its normal state; then fill with wool, and leave it in for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	When the forearm bone of a man or woman is fractured, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and these fractures do not usually remain hidden, for they proceed from those who study and use it, and they are mentioned in my book. For a fracture signifies that there are several ways to restore it: therefore take heed.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is fractured, take a goose neck and bind it up; then cover it with cloth, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be perfectly healed then.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as for the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it should be sound now, if what we have said is true
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, if the clot of vitriol remains, if you have nothing else, then resume the fracture in the same hour, or the following, if there is no other sign of fracture.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is swelling at the fracture, if the swelling persists until the next day, leave the restoration until the swelling has subsided, and do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will risk causing further damage.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is fractured and is apparent through the skin, cover it immediately with your hands, lightly extending your fingers.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if extension does not appear to you, hold this instrument of iron, which is about the length of three or four fingers, and its width is according to the extent of the wound; for this reason it is necessary to press three or four fingers, according to what is necessary in the wound of a fracture; and let it be round and firm, so that it does not press against the limb at your work, or be placed before and behind, and large in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called "palainche" because it is necessary to place the curved limb upon the head of the fractured bone; and once it has been placed, it must be even so that one side meets the other. And if the fracture is slight, and the instrument does not well grasp the bone, if you press the head of the bone, while the instrument still has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you grasp with a covering instrument that can reach that area, or if you must incision or burn, at your peril; then withdraw that which is remaining embedded in the bone, with rough rasps and scanty pus.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is restored, and the patient experiences great pain afterwards, swelling that is not in its natural position. If you do too much to restore it, then moisten with black vinegar, and do so cautiously; do not put anything else on the wound except oil, for it will cause decay and corruption; then administer stars when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the bursting; for many times this has been done foolishly, and it has caused the patient to die or become lame or corrupt many times; let the inflammation be milder and more delicate than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if it is not necessary to put on stars; but wrap around, instead of stars, a firm cloth, and bind them. And when you see afterwards that it is swelling more or less, if that which you put on has become soft, and there is healing wound, like ointment tetrafarmaçon and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must stretch the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is soldered and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And you must keep the limb perfectly still in some measure that it can move easily without causing harm
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it is dislocated again, and it cannot stay in place, it must be reset while the limb is still slightly bent, as there are small pieces of bone that must be broken in order to stop the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If a fistula arises in the limb, or any other kind of corruption, if you must cure it, according to what is said in this chapter above. And when the bone is broken, and opened on the limb, as for example the bones of the thigh or the shoulder, and other large bones, if you do not treat them, many times death comes from this. But leave them as long as they bleed; perhaps by chance it will heal by itself after twenty or thirty days, and then cure the wound if you wish; or if you do not wish, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The hairs which come out from the beard
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The hairs which come out from the beard come out many times after the heat of the summer, even when it is close to the joint, and it is a helpful thing to see how the limb is positioned; and by chance it cannot do its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Beware then that you take care: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and the like, do not take any of these things, or all of them together, and mix them with wine that is astringent or with plenty of egg or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then dislocate it, and do it again, until the dislocations are bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it hardens all the swellings under the limb; and if the dislocation has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above has burst, and to make the excess apparent; or you leave it without a drain, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored, and hangs limp after the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it: because it was too tightly bound and was not bound properly; or because there are too many bands, and cannot come back to the limb naturally; or because of many wounds; or from too great movements, not even in its proper place; or because there is much blood in its body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make the limb firm, as long as it does not swell in him; and give him bath, and make him joyful and cheerful; then put on a bandage over the limb, so that the bandage attracts to great nourishment, and the blood flows often hot, until the nourishment comes back to the limb; and restore it to its natural position.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the illness.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is bent after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, all this without damaging its natural work: for it is not believed that one should break the limb anew, as some fools say; and many have suffered from this treatment in our land; this work is blamed, and many deaths result from it; however, if the swelling and pain are fresh, if you can raise them with warm water or soft herbs, such as meadowsweet leaves, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and you make a soft dressing, like with aquaint well done, and take the nourishing draught of meadowsweet, and mix it with grease of gelline or olive oil, and make a dressing on top; or you take fat figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that alleviate the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never should the bone be dislocated by continuous rubbing and for a long time with wet hands. And give the limb a gentle movement every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron tongs, if you cover it up to the bone, make a superficial incision; and put cushion and packing in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron tongs, if you cover it up to the bone, make a superficial incision; and put cushion and packing in the wound.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no avail, if it can now be remedied.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is late, and if the limb is swollen, and by chance we reset it, we have pricked the limb at its root; for this reason we must not move it while it is swollen: many times it has caused swelling and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Whenever this happens, if the patient is made whole, then let him rest; until the swelling subsides; then raise the limb high and with oil, and move it gently, and cure each limb as it comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning dislocations from the shoulder to the foot
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jaws are loosened and the dislocation of both is like this: when they are united to their bones, and softened by moisture; or when they are entirely loosened, and hang towards the chin, and close the mouth that it cannot hold it, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, if it returns by itself in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accompanied, if you must, to hold it fast, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such manner that the minister holds the head of the sufferer, and look that you put your hand on the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible in the mouth, if the dislocation is of one and a half parts; and the other hand must be loosened, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And look that you make the thing even, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arise with hot water and oil, keep them lightly; do not force the return, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back even, and the patient’s mouth is closed, and feeling well, put upon damp cloths moistened in cerote made of rose oil and wax, then bind loosely with fine thread.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient sleeps on his back, and his arms rest between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, do not attempt to straighten, but grasp lightly meat, until the pains are overcome, and the teeth are quiet;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then eat what he wants lightly, and do not work too hard to open the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well quiet and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the jaw bones do not manage to be reset at a single hour, and are not firmly converted to their place, then fever and swelling become accustomed, and by chance solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see that, then know that it is a loss; and many times death is the consequence in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove the bone from its place without causing further damage, and is always damaging when it is used.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And if the patient lies prone on his back, extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then place the bandage and the dressing, and strain it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the one who is beside the knee cannot unbuckle; if it does not, and if it unbuckles once, if you hold it firmly, as we have said; then place the dressing and the bandage, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the limb is brought back to its place, when it is relieved from its limb.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	De la dislocation de l’espaule.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated by moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with a slight movement as we have experienced, then it is necessary to first reset the dislocation.
