et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it is not loosened behind by the shoulder, and is not loosened within by the nerves; and several times it is loosened below towards the shoulder, even among those who have much hair, for among those who have enough hair, there are prickles, and they return with prickles.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, there happen to be blows or fractures, and swell the shoulder from a deep abscess, and care that it is loosened by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must certainly be sure, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation is when it is turned towards the shoulder, and distinguishes between the diseased and the healthy shoulder, and you will find between their diversity a visible difference;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a cavity, and the arm hangs down from the shoulder, as if it were a bow; and the patient cannot move his hand back to its place, or move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And thus, if it is displaced upwards, if not hidden, for you will find it clearly on palpation.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not forced to restore it, when it is new, or if the limb is painful.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the assistant holds the painful limb upwards, then places his thumbs below the armpit, and holds the joint forcefully upwards; and the assistant holds the limb, and extends it upwards, because it is put below; if necessary.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said above, if it is to be known that the patient is to be bathed in warm water; and it is administered soft and soothing nourishment, such as decoction of heliotrope and fennel and honey in water, and is administered;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then, if necessary, soothe the patient on his back, and put on the seat of the assle a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, then put the eye of the thumb on the cushion, and keep the head of the shoulder firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another minister holds the head of the patient firmly, if it does not move downwards; the shoulder will return immediately. If you see that it remains dislocated in this way,
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that you make yourself present, that is to say, someone who is greater than the patient; and that you place two fingers against the cost of the shoulder, and keep the shoulder depressed by the patient’s hand, so that the patient’s arm hangs down
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister treats the hand of the patient backward toward the belly. And if the patient is too light, if he can bear nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And we must also remember in another way: if the bone is fixed, that is to say, long as a nail in the earth, from which the head of the shoulder must not be too great or too small; ...
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then put on the patient’s hand, but that it be covered with coarse cloth, and that the patient’s hand be placed long enough; then stretch out the hand backward from the other side, and the dislocation will return to its place immediately; ...
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	If these things fail to restore it, if you wish to perform this cure: take one thumb and two fingers of great length, which have the tip rounded like a mouse entering through an opening in the wall, and place them under the armpit, following this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	If these things fail to restore it, if you wish to perform this cure: take one thumb and two fingers of great length, which have the tip rounded like a mouse entering through an opening in the wall, and place them under the armpit, following this form. Then support the shoulder with a cloth, so that it does not bleed the patient, and place it under the armpit of the patient. Extend your arms above the shoulder, and support the arm at the wrist, and place the thumb on the index finger of a fist, and extend the hand outward. The joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way, if you wish to keep it in place, put under the armpit a square ball of wool of equal size, and put on it a pad of powdered meal, with incense and alum of egg, on the whole shoulder and around the joint, then strain under the armpit immediately, and keep the limb resting on the pad, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still together.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move the limb gently while it is comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then move it more vigorously after five or six days, and move it. And if it is stiff and cannot be softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stiff due to moisture from the beginning, or for another cause, if it is necessary, administer two punctures with the cautery, as is often done before or alongside cautery procedures.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and the joint remains dislocated after six days, and the limb still cannot be raised, then the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and if the joint never heals in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The shoulder dislocation which is from the front, and the arm, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and is administered with another bandage; and it heals as long as it is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes pain in the limb, and later movement, if the patient uses the limb many times, as long as that pain is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation that remains.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint is dislocated at the point where it is usually stable, and the same thing happens at the front and the back; and it is often detached, both front and back, and the dislocation is not easily remedied, for we see it clearly and feel it well; and it is detached in this way.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the patient with a bandage, if he can see it openly. For the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm, touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And must keep it still as before, because if it were to come loose again, if it should ever happen, it will bring grief to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back whole, even if it is at the back; for it is better to leave it as it is than to cause further pain, and by chance there comes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is restored again, when it is such that it can be brought back, you must extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down to the level of the patient's shoulders front and back, and hold the joint firmly together, or at the root of the bone, until it returns to its place
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when the patient doubles their hand over their hand, and grasps from the root of the thumb which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it firmly, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the armpit, and wrap around a double-length and wide bandage;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when you have looked at the joint at the hand, if the limb is devoid of any oil to soften the joint, then stretch the joint firmly, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, if you put on a dry plaster with a piece of egg, and it strains, and bends the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it for some days, then take it off.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	When the joint is firmly in its place, if you loosen the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the plastering and the limb, and leave it until it is firmly set; then take it off.</start_of_turn>
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if there is pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe and massage it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a greasy poultice of mutton, then leave it for a day and a night, then take out the poultice and the bone, and do the same.</start_of_turn
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	When he sweats, let him wipe the joint gently; then reset the nail on, and then put in or bathe; do this three or four times until he is healed.  If you see that there is excessive moisture in the sweat, add ashes to the bath; this will absorb the moisture.
li dislocation de la main	When the hand is dislocated...
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	When the joint of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more so than the others, it must be immediately reset in its place without delay, even if there is swelling or if there is a fracture.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And if you put your hand on a table, and extend your arm, and look at it so that you see that you put your palm on the surface of the joint, and hold it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must look to see if it is well in place; then put your hand behind your back on a table when extending and returning it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the arm, if you put your hand behind your back on the table, and look to see that you put your hand on that surface of the joint. If it returns now, it is well.</start_of_turn>
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of the calming patches is excessive, let them be removed and leave in their place.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not wish to keep it in after a while, the joint will remain broken
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	neither does it harm the patient more than that his hands are relaxed, and cannot do anything: because if the nerves are cut or the vein is severed, except for the case of cautery, nothing else is worth doing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in place, if you put on the dressing that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it easily, and there is no pain, if the wound is filled with warm liquid, and it is washed until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	et le laisse ainsi trois jours, et puis le met égal celui jour; et de ne pas le lier, si comme nous l’avons dit, et garder des yeux ouverts, et ne le fasse pas bouger, et le serre lier de nouveau; et fais ceci souvent, tant qu’il soit étroit.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and leave it thus for three days, and then put it equal today; and do not bind it, as we have said, and keep the eyes open, and do not move it, and bind it again; and do this often, until it is narrow.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	and do the same if it is dislocated at the wrist, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated from another part.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or the collarbone is loosened, or if there are several loosenings, if no remedy is found, for the patient is in haste.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	When the swelling leaps forward, it cannot be held back, and many times it softens no limb, or the knees or arms or legs.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the shoulder blade turns three times; that which turns behind is called "gilbosite."
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The cure is that if the gilbosite comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of all.</start_of_turn>
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from sitting or impacts or similar things, say the old methods of treatment with great words, or there is no benefit at all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes before the wound, there is no healing at all;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly at the cost, and one cannot cure it but what comes from behind, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And let the patient keep his face stretched out one inch above the level, and have tension from his eyes, that he does not move;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then hold one thumb at the top of the limb in the earth forms, and one at the toes, and bind one thread beside the patient’s armpits, and one at the waist, and one at the hips, and one at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two assistants know the threads, one at the top and the other at the toes, among the three thumbs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And be well closed, the thumb as we have said, and look that he puts his palms on the spine forms, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	If she does not return by this treatment, take two fingers of length, and hold them against the side, and let the patient lie on his side; put the thumb against the side, then put the middle of the thumb on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	Put the thumbs over the other thumb, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not work, do it with the pin that is at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And put four stitches at the head of the patient’s arm of great length, and between each stitch, a knot and a thread, a palm of space of length.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And every basin has one opening, or the tube turns crooked, and let the basin be firmly fixed in the earth, if it does not move; and between every two basins there is one basin returning, so that when the thread returns, there are in two returns two small basins of a palm's length, to bring back the tube.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then the thread which is among the knots towards the head, and the other thread towards the pieces at the other end, and let the basins turn their tube throughout the thread, and the master puts the thorn even as we have said
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put upon a dry dressing with abundance of eggs, and then press, and then support with a tablet of two thumbs, that it may cover the root of the pain and the part of the ribcage that is painful, and then tie with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient’s natural nourishment, until it is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if nothing else comes to pass at the end of the sickness, if it is commanded to administer soothing and calming medicines, with the exception that we have said before; and in no case shall a piece of lead be administered.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And never let the appearance of a swelling on the back of the neck be seen as anything other than a dislocation; for it is the bone that opens, from which we must not presume: by chance death will come.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Hairs that are attached to the hip and shoulder joints only become loose from dislocations alone, and do not come out with other joints; and the hip joint is loosened in three parts: within and without, and in front and behind; and the more within it is loosened, the more loosened is in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of dislocation within is that when one joins the painful limb with the tendon, if it is longer, and if the patient groans more than before, and cannot bend the limb at the joint to the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	then it is the bruise that is left behind from the cautery, because the head of the humerus comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes to the aid, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one who comes to the aid, if it is that he has his limb well in accordance with the accomplishment; however, do not double his knee with pain, and if you see him do so, do not do so before, and retain his urine, and swell his groin, and when he walks, pass over his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one who comes to the aid, if it is that he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and is that his limb is shorter than the other, and his groin is softened, and his shoulder is dislocated from its socket
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	You must take back this semblance of dislocation if it is an old dislocation and it remains according to its habit, if there is no cure; and it is not recommended that you do so unless there is presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty you will twist the joint, and stretch outwards and downwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, if you must, apply one strong minister, and stretch the limb firmly with both hands, or with one hand that is sufficient to bind it on the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another minister extends his hand downwards in part as much as he can stretch out his hands downwards from his ankles, then bind it with a loop of thread above the hip; and another holds the head of the limb.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And extend upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	Such a method of extension is common in three out of four cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If this does not suffice, if you deem it necessary, you must put a cure in place. When the dislocation is at the shoulder, you must first elevate the patient above his costal margin, then place the limb on the root of the scapula, and that which is below the elbow, and extend the limb upwards towards the armpit, and downwards towards the forcele.</start_of_turn>
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then grasp another assistant to support his arms, and embrace the thick limb of the afflicted shoulder, and extend it outward: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is less laborious than the others.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	If you do not manage to bind the shoulder firmly in this manner as we have said, if you know that the patient has a severe pain in his limbs, bind his arms together with a strong thread around his thumbs and his knees, and let the affected limb hang down more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then let the limb hang from the shoulder, or suspend it from the ground for the length of two arms; then command the minister to grasp the shoulder joint, and let another minister stand beside the patient, who graspes the shoulder, for the joint has now returned normally.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is overcome, if the patient is lying down, as we have said in the case of dislocation, grasp the limb firmly with one hand, and on the foot as well;

But if not, put on his table, and press on it as we said in the treatise, and keep the patient lying on the side of the cost.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, if you must, extend the limb gently, as I have said; and look with your eyes where the pain is on the painful side, and press on the other hand, and extend it backwards towards the groin.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the shoulder, if it does not suffice to extend the patient forward, do not lift him up from the ground, but rather that he remain as if he had been loosened at the shoulder, as we have said above concerning the two thumbs.

et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if it rests two or three days, then loosen it, and place the bandage upon it; and if you see that they are even, if it has strained as before, leave it. For two days; then loosen it, and make it comfortable without delay, until the limb is restored to its normal position.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the shoulder joint...
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint is dislocated in two ways: forward and backward; and do not strain it forward
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that if you instruct the patient to bend his limb at the knee, and it does not reach his buttock, it is a sign that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and restore all of them if you make the patient sit upright, and extend his limb if he can, and put your hand behind his face, and put his heel on your toes

And place the padding on, and raise the limb to the hip, and bind them together firmly for two or three days, then remove it.  Do not let the patient move until the limb is comfortable.

de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The shoulder is never completely rigid and is always somewhat dislocated and painful.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and that it has been displaced beforehand to the part where it is loosened.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	If the lameness is slight, it must be gently extended with the hands when it is only slightly swollen
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is thoroughly dry, it is necessary to make the patient sit upright, and hold him, that is to say support him strongly under the arm, below the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then draw the limb towards your right hand, and then towards the left hand twice, and then extend it upwards, and hold it firmly;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	et fai ce trois fois, si com nos avons dit, en monast et en traiant le pied; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it does not return, make the patient lie on his back on the earth, and hold one foot firmly in the earth between his thighs, and bind a bandage around it, so that he does not bleed the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then hold the shoulder steady, and another attendant extends the limb with his hands or with something, which is placed on the collar of the limb;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend the chest muscles equally, and hold them either apart between the knees of the patient to keep the patient steady when extending.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the eyes equally on the dislocation at his hands, and another minister grasps the limb firmly at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it returns to a point, if you put on the dressing and press upon it, and the strain is complete, and you bind the limb to the limb, and keep the nerves that are above the ankle behind, that they are not too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for one or two days, and if the strain is gone; then loosen the bandage at one-third or one-fourth, and send the patient away after three days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	If he goes before that end, it is not my certainty that he will not be spoiled again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he pricks at his base, if you must hold his eyes still as we have said before, until he is whole again.</start_of_turn>
des dois	until he is healed.</start_of_turn>
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if you can gently stretch the limb, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in no other place but at the back of the shoulder, it is advised that you make the patient sit upright on a chair or on the bed, and place your hand on what is open of these joints, then press your hand firmly until it returns to its place.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is equal, and there is no opening, if you put the hand of the arm on a table at the shoulder, then press firmly, and leave it for two days, then release it; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	with wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not cautious in the cure, and you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be rash;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning soothing things appostomately, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if you now restore the limb to its place, even if the swelling remains;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is at rest, if necessary, administer calming things around the wound, and cure the wound if possible, with dried sponges.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	If the dislocation has burst, and softer bones are fractured, if the bones are flexible, do as is said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	Beware of entering a state of fear, as I have already said, for this brings danger to both your soul and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Explain the physical symptom.
